Page 7

Funeral of Hu Hanmin: Central Representative Sun Ke Presided Over the Solemn Ceremony; Over 120,000 People from Chinese and Foreign Circles Attended

Guangzhou Dispatch: The remains of the late Standing Committee Member and Chairman of the Fifth Central Executive Committee of the Kuomintang, Hu Hanmin, were given a state funeral in Guangdong on the 25th of this month. In advance, central officials, representatives from various provinces, and representatives from overseas party branches arrived in Guangzhou to participate in the ceremony. The Office of the State Funeral of Chairman Hu also made advance preparations for all state funeral matters. The cemetery was solemnly decorated, and the ceremonies on the day of the state funeral were orderly and well-organized. Details are listed as follows:

Cemetery Scene

Hu's cemetery is located on Lion Mountain in Douwenlang, Longyandong, in Panyu County, a suburb of Guangzhou. The cemetery and the avenue leading to the tomb were completed several months ago. Two large temporary sheds were erected in front of the tomb to serve as the venue for the state funeral ceremony. Potted flowers were displayed on both sides of the avenue, and triangular flags of alternating black and white colors were planted. At the entrance to the avenue, there was a plain archway over ten feet high, with the four characters "精神不死" ("Spirit Never Dies") written on it. Further in, there were two more archways, one with the inscription "天下楷模" ("Model for the World") and the other with "薄海同悲" ("All Seas Mourn"), both grand in appearance. At the end of the archways, there were three halls. The central hall served as a reception area for various organizations and groups. The halls on the left and right served as rest areas for overseas party representatives and school representatives. Condolence banners and eulogies were hung all around, from high-ranking officials of the central government to relatives and old friends, all sending condolences in black characters on white cloth. Next to the reception area were the military police stations and officers' rest areas. Entering from the reception area was the memorial hall. Above the hall was a plaque with the inscription "胡主席國葬典禮" ("State Funeral Ceremony of Chairman Hu") written horizontally. The interior of the hall was decorated with black and white cloth balls and condolence banners. In the center was a portrait of Chairman Hu, with the party and national emblem hanging behind it. In front of the portrait was a long table with offerings and flowers, as well as a giant bronze tripod engraved with the characters "不匱" ("Inexhaustible"), a gift from Wang Longzhai.

State Funeral Ceremony

Central officials paying respects to Hu (photographed by Zhen Jing)

The day before, people from all walks of life went to the State Funeral Office to receive attendance certificates, bus tickets, and Hu commemorative items, including a porcelain statue of Chairman Hu, a collection of poems from the Inexhaustible Room, and a commemorative badge. Those who came to pay respects from private groups or organizations received bus tickets. Therefore, on the 25th, at dawn, those attending the ceremony went in an endless stream. The Panyu Highway was crowded with plain cars and white horses. Before 8 a.m., there were no empty seats at the reception. Soon, central representatives and representatives from various provinces arrived one after another, including Chairman Lin Sen of the Central Government, Sun Ke (acting on behalf), central representatives Lin Yunhai, Wang Chonghui, Li Wenfan, Shao Yuanchong, Jiao Yitang, Liu Guanxun, Zhu Hezhong, Fu Bingchang, Chen Lifu, Liang Hancao, representatives from various ministries and departments Shi Ying, Zheng Hongnian, Huang Musong, Xie Wuliang, Wang Yongbin, Zhang Yuanyou, Liu Weichi, Yun Yingqiao, Luo Gang, Xiong Mengbin representing Feng Yuxiang, Li Hongwen representing Yan Xishan, Zhang Renmin and Li Renren representing Li Zongren and Bai Chongxi of Guangxi, Guangdong Pacification Director Yu Hanmou, as well as Guangdong department heads, senior officers from the Fourth Route Army, representatives from party branches in various provinces and cities, representatives from overseas party branches, representatives from various people's organizations, representatives from various schools, foreign guests including consuls (or representatives of their respective ambassadors) from Britain, France, Germany, Japan, Norway, Sweden, Switzerland, Portugal, Finland, Denmark, Czech Republic, etc. stationed in Guangdong, and people from all walks of life who voluntarily participated, numbering no less than 120,000. At noon, the ceremony began. The first row in the center of the hall was the seating for the central presiding officials, the first row on the left side was the seating for central committee members, government members, and central representatives, the second row was the seating for heads of various ministries and departments, the third row was the seating for representatives from overseas party branches and consuls from various countries, the first row on the right side was the seating for ambassadors or representatives from various countries, the second row was the seating for party, government, and military heads and committee members from various provinces and cities, and the third row was the seating for members of the State Funeral Office. Following that were the seating for representatives from various organizations, groups, and schools. After taking their places, incense and candles were lit in front of the hall. The scene was solemn, with the smoke of incense curling upward. Central Representative Sun Ke presided over the ceremony, and mourning music was played. After the music stopped, the presiding officials offered flowers and respectfully read the eulogy from the central government and the government of each province, as well as eulogies from various parties (read by Zhu Shouyu, Secretary of the Guangdong Provincial Government). After the reading, the music began again, and the entire assembly bowed three times to the portrait of the deceased. After the bowing, there was three minutes of silence. Then, the ceremony of adding soil was held. Led by Sun Ke, central officials Lin Yunhai, Shao Yuanchong, Li Wenfan, etc. proceeded to the side of Hu's tomb, took a handful of soil, and scattered it in front of the grave. After the sealing of the tomb, they returned to their original positions and bowed three times to the portrait of the deceased. At this time, Hu's widow, Chen Shuzi, and daughter, Hu Mulan, wept loudly in the mourning curtain. Many of those who attended were moved to tears. The crowd then withdrew amid the final mourning music. At this time, people from all walks of life who came to pay their respects freely were coming and going in an endless stream, which did not end until 2 p.m.

City Mourning

Chairman Hu's cemetery (photographed by Zhen Jingyan)

During the moment of silence at the state funeral ceremony, all the lights in the city were turned on, factories sounded their sirens, and citizens all stood silently for three minutes. At the same time, the Humen Fort fired 101 gun salutes to express mourning. All shops, government offices, and schools flew flags at half-mast. Theaters, cinemas, and entertainment venues were closed for the day, and music was suspended to express mourning. In addition, two unfortunate incidents occurred on this day. One was that Luo Peizhi, a veteran revolutionary party member, committed suicide by slitting his throat with a knife at the public memorial venue. Luo was a member of the Overseas Comrades Society and a native of Panyu County, Guangdong. In his early years, he was a businessman in Longjibao, Nanyang, and was friendly with Yun Lie and others. He followed Sun Yat-sen to engage in the revolution. Later, he returned to China after his business failed. He repeatedly decided to start an uprising in China. He was upright and did not seek power or influence. After the success of the revolution, he still earned his own living. In his later years, his family was impoverished and lacked assistance. He became increasingly frustrated. Fellow comrades in Guangdong occasionally provided assistance, but after Hu Hanmin's death, the assistance from all parties was cut off. Luo had no way to support himself. On this day, after paying respects to Hu, he felt emotional about his own life and committed suicide with a knife in front of the cemetery. Fortunately, he was rescued and sent to the hospital for treatment. His life was not in danger. This is one incident. On the same day, a group of about 20 people who came to pay their respects to Hu took public bus No. 7024 to Lion Mountain. While passing in front of the Yantang Military Academy, due to the jostling of the crowd, the driver was momentarily careless, and the entire bus fell into a pool of water. Three women surnamed Zhang and Liang and a man surnamed Huang were seriously injured. It was reported that they were representatives of a certain labor union. Six or seven others were slightly injured. After receiving medical treatment, most of them recovered. This is another incident. (October 26th)

Zhejiang Province: New Long-Distance Telephone Facilities; Installation of Carrier Telephony and Addition of Amplifiers

Hangzhou Dispatch: The construction of long-distance telephones in our country's provinces began earliest in Zhejiang Province, and the density of the Qian lines and the completion of the telephone communication network have also become the crown of various provinces. This is due to the careful planning and efforts of the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Authorities and those in charge over the years. I recently heard that although there are several pairs of direct lines between Hangzhou and Yongjia, and between Hangzhou and Yin County, the telephone traffic is congested, and the original Qian lines are no longer sufficient. In order to remedy this, after planning everything, the Zhejiang Provincial Construction Department approved the purchase of carrier equipment from the German Siemens factory, to be installed in Hangzhou, Yongjia, and Yin County respectively. After installation, with the help of carrier action, one pair of telephone lines can have the communication function of two pairs of telephone lines, and it can be expanded in the future. The cost of this equipment is more than twice as much as adding lines. In order to improve the efficiency of inter-provincial calls, the bureau also decided to install long-distance amplifiers in Hangzhou, Lanxi, Yongjia, Ningbo, and other four places to make the sound transmission of calls clear and loud everywhere. The two amplifiers in Hangzhou have already been installed and are working perfectly. It is now known that the bureau is also installing a 22-type amplifier each in Lanxi and Yongjia. The machine has also been ordered from the German Siemens factory, and it will soon be shipped to Hangzhou for installation and standby. After that, the communication in Zhejiang Province will be more smooth than before. According to the carrier telephone equipment, the cost is low and the efficiency is high. Many European and American countries have adopted it. It is still a new idea in China. This move by the bureau has created a new record in China's telecommunications facilities. In the future, as the telephone business develops in various provinces, this facility will inevitably be imitated and adopted by the construction authorities of various provinces.

Songjiang: Machine Presentation Representative Goes to Beijing

The 31st is the 50th birthday of Chairman Chiang. The agencies and groups of the province raised funds to purchase a plane to present to the government, and held a presentation ceremony on that day. All counties sent representatives to participate in the grand ceremony. Our county has appointed Cheng Weiru and Lu Shulian as representatives of our county, and they went to Beijing yesterday.

Water Patrol Team Arrests Notorious Bandit

The water patrol team was ordered to go on patrol. The team leader Fei Gongxia led the patrol boat to tour Punan a few days ago. It was reported that Yang Ayuan, the former member of the already executed bandit leader Li Jinxiang, has recently been hiding in Shanyang. The team immediately led the team to arrest him and found a lotus pistol and more than 30 rounds of box gun ammunition in his home. He was brought back to the team headquarters for interrogation yesterday. The suspect confessed that he was 26 years old and from Pankushiang in the eighth district. He has committed many robberies in Punan. However, the suspect has many accomplices, and they are currently being pursued in order to eliminate the banditry.

Suzhou: Teacher-Student Love Suicide Case

Chen Tianyi, 35, from Wujiang, is the nephew of the late Chen Qubing. He used to be a teacher at Jiangsu Provincial Women's Vocational School in Suzhou. He had a teacher-student relationship with female student Wang Yifen. After the incident, Chen resigned due to the incident, and the woman also dropped out of school. Later, Chen took a job as a teacher at Shanghai Huinan Middle School in Shanghai and lured the woman to Shanghai to study at the school. After Wang's father, Zai Bohua, reported the matter to the Shanghai authorities, the school dismissed Chen and Wang. They temporarily stayed at the Yuanyuan Hotel on Second Avenue in Shanghai. Later, Wang Yifen realized Chen's deception and returned to Suzhou on the 6:15 pm train from Shanghai on the 28th. Chen also tracked down to Suzhou on the same train. Because Chen did not purchase a ticket, the ticket inspector discovered him. At this time, Wang Yifen said that she did not know Chen Tianyi, so the train inspector felt even more suspicious and was questioning them separately. Near Anting, Wang Yifen suddenly jumped off the train and attempted suicide. She survived, and then jumped into a pond next to the road. The train stopped and the train inspector got off the train and entered the pond to rescue her. She was brought to Suzhou and sent to the Gospel Hospital for treatment. She only suffered a slight head injury and was not in danger of life. Chen Tianyi was sent to the police station and transferred to the Public Security Bureau for interrogation.

Lawyer Impersonates Civil Servant

Lawyer Qian Jiazhen was accused of obstructing order by impersonating a bailiff to seal up a house while handling a case of inheritance of temple property for Taoist Mao Zhongqing and Yin Fuyuan. The local court has sentenced him to a fine of 100 yuan. Qian refused to accept the verdict and prepared to appeal to the High Court.

Kunshan: Rural Gambling Resurges

Gambling has always been rampant in the county. County Magistrate Peng Baichuan strictly banned rural teahouses as soon as he took office, hoping to curb gambling. Recently, when the new grain was on the market, some local ruffians took the opportunity to sneak into the countryside to lure farmers to gamble in order to reap profits. In recent days, they have been discovered in various villages in the fourth district. Farmers are willing to bet all their hard-earned money. It is hoped that the authorities will pay attention to strict prohibition.

Prolonged Drought

Since the beginning of autumn, there has been no rain in the county for more than two months. The fields are cracked, and all the villages are suffering from drought. The rice stem borers are active, and the late rice harvest is bound to be greatly reduced. Winter crops cannot be planted, and farmers are worried.

Wuxi: Appeals for Explanation of Cocoon Prices

The Jiangsu Provincial Cocoon Industry Association, the Wuxi Cocoon Trade Association, and the Silk Factory Association suffered heavy losses due to the two different autumn cocoon prices set by the previous improvement association. They sent a telegram to the Construction Department to appeal and express the plight of the silk and cocoon industry. They subsequently received instructions from the department, but the doubts were not fully resolved. Yesterday, they submitted another report to the department, requesting an explanation on three points: (1) The two different autumn cocoon prices this year are due to the government's abnormal orders and merchants' huge losses. Does the three-grade standard cocoon price set by the National Economic Council's Silk Improvement Committee have the power to bind Jiangsu? Is Jiangsu within the scope of the country? (2) The Cocoon Leaf Improvement Management Committee stipulated that the cocoon price must not be lower than 29 yuan. However, the products have their own prices. High-quality goods are reeled at 400 catties, and defective goods are reeled at 500 catties. The minimum price must not be less than 29 yuan, that is, defective cocoons should also be purchased at 29 yuan. Any nitpicking is extortion and will be severely punished. Government officials speak as government officials, and merchants speak as merchants. The positions are different, but the principles are the same. Is it fair? (3) Recently, President Zeng frequently relied on his personal opinions and acted arbitrarily. Merchants occasionally made requests, and either said it was difficult to handle or said it should not be discussed. He acted arrogantly and disregarded everything. Is it legal according to the constitution?

Qingwu Road to be Completed

The Qingwu Road from Qingyangzhen in Jiangyin to Wujin has been under construction since March this year. More than half a year has passed, and all the projects such as the roadbed, bridges, and culverts have been completed. The crushed stone pavement is now being laid. Because the contractors are facing a tight deadline, the work is intense, and even gasoline lamps are lit to work overnight. The eastern section of the road has been paved to the 21st bridge, and the western section has been paved to the 18th bridge at the southern end of Qinan in the ninth district of Xishu. Only three kilometers have not yet been paved. It is expected that it will be fully completed by the end of this month and open to traffic. The Construction Department will send personnel to inspect and accept the project after the end of the month.

Changzhou: Tuberculosis Prevention Department Implements Lung Examination

The Wuyi Red Swastika Society Hospital has a tuberculosis prevention X-ray department. In addition to the registration fee, each person who goes for a lung examination will only be charged one yuan, middle school students will be charged eight jiao, and elementary school students will be charged six jiao. The fee will be collected from November 1st, every Sunday morning until 11:00 am, with a limit of 20 people each time. The hospital also has the Majishan Lung Disease Sanatorium, which has already opened. The address is Fenghuangling, Guzhu Xiang, surrounded by lakes, fresh air, perfect facilities, and low fees.

Jiangyin: Police Officer Shot While Arresting Gamblers

Since the new grains have been on the market, the peasants of the various villages all use the excuse of gambling to have a good time. Patrol Officer Dong Daguang of the first police station of the South Suburb Public Security Bureau learned that there was a gambling den at the Sheyuan Sanbao Shidun Convent and led the police to the scene. Unexpectedly, there were more than 80 gamblers. Most of them escaped, and only nine people including the owner, Jin Ziwen, were arrested. In the confusion, police officer Yao Wenyun's box gun went off and the bullet pierced his right foot. The gamblers were sent to the county for trial and sentencing on the 28th. The injured policeman was sent to Jiangyin Hospital. In the afternoon, Shen, the prosecutor, went to examine the injury. The condition did not look serious.

Yangzhou: Raising Funds to Purchase Grain for Famine Relief

The Jiangdu County Government convened a food management committee on the afternoon of the 28th, and decided to raise 20,000 yuan to purchase grain to store for famine relief. Zhou Guren, Zhu Ganchen, Zhang Ganting, Yu Peiren, and Zhu Lizun were appointed as the five members responsible for handling the matter.

Ningbo: Money Houses Handling the Collection of Funds

The money houses in this city, having extended long-term credit to industrial and commercial firms in Shanghai, with the deadline of November 10th approaching, have been sending personnel to Shanghai in recent days to handle the collection of funds. Those with established credit are being granted extensions until May 10th of next year. The internal trading rate for this period is five yuan and five jiao per thousand yuan. The total amount of loans issued by various firms is reportedly similar to the previous period, remaining around ten million yuan. The issue of long-term loans in this city has also begun to be handled, making the workload of various firms quite busy lately.

Impending Drought Threatens to Become a Disaster

The counties under the jurisdiction of Ningbo are mostly mountainous, with relatively few fields. Agricultural crops rely heavily on rainfall. Since the beginning of autumn, there has been no rain for two months, making the drought particularly severe. As a result, rivers have dried up, making navigation difficult and irrigation water sources scarce. If it does not rain soon, it will inevitably lead to a very serious drought disaster.

Shaoxing: Fire at Baoyou Bridge

A fire broke out under Baoyou Bridge in Shaoxing at approximately 1:00 AM on the 27th. It originated in the Jiuhua Oil Candle Shop. Because the shop was filled with flammable materials, once ignited, it was impossible to control. After firefighters from various volunteer groups arrived and worked to extinguish the blaze, it was finally put out. It is estimated that five or six businesses were destroyed, including the Ding Hexing Niangao Shop, Qingxiang Fruit Shop, and Yuanxing Wine and Sauce Shop, along with more than ten houses.

Cixi: Exemption of Public Land Tax

In the past, this county acquired much civilian land for the construction of the Ciyang Road and the excavation of the Xiaoxi Dike. The landowners repeatedly petitioned for exemption from land taxes. After receiving the petitions, the county government had a map drawn up and submitted it to the provincial government for review. Yesterday, an order was received stating that because this civilian land was acquired for public use, it should be exempt from property taxes. After receiving the order, the county government has instructed the collection office to proceed accordingly.

Hangzhou: Major Fire on Qingtai Road Yesterday Morning

At 4:55 AM on the 29th, a fire suddenly broke out at the Taihe Clothing Store at No. 305 Qingtai Road in Hangzhou due to a short circuit in the storage area. The fire quickly spread. The store's employees were awakened from their sleep and quickly called the fire department, which dispatched fire trucks to the scene. It took more than an hour to extinguish the blaze. It is estimated that five buildings and clothing goods were destroyed, with total losses exceeding 40,000 yuan. The store had fire insurance for 20,000 yuan. The accountant, Pan Wenyou, has been detained by the Public Security Bureau for questioning.

Panic Over Drinking Water in the City

Since the beginning of autumn, Hangzhou has experienced a long period of sunny weather with no rain for nearly two months. Rivers and drinking wells have gradually dried up. Inland river boats can hardly pass. City residents must rely on tap water for drinking water, leading to a sharp increase in tap water users. The required amount of tap water during the peak summer season is 1.3 million gallons per day. However, the daily demand for water in autumn has reached 1.7 million gallons, which is beyond expectations. Moreover, the only source of tap water is the nearby Tiesha River. The river water level has already dropped by three feet. If it does not rain for another half month, the drinking water problem in the city will become quite difficult.

Recent Overview of Guangdong and Guangxi (11)

— Our reporter Xiao An

Visits to Various Important People

After arriving at the headquarters of the Fourth Group Army, Commander-in-Chief Li DeLin immediately granted an audience and spoke freely for an hour before concluding. Afterward, a visit was made to Vice Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Group Army Bai JianSheng, with another hour of discussion. Subsequently, visits were made to Provincial Chairman Huang XuChu, Central Committee Members Li RenRen and Liu LuYin, Political Training Director of the Fourth Group Army Pan YiZhi, Provincial Party Committee Member Huang JunDa, Nanning District Civil Corps Commander Liang HanSong, Chief of Staff Fan YuFeng, former Special Envoy for Foreign Affairs in the Five Southwestern Provinces Gan JieHou, and Nanning Republic Daily President Hu NeSheng, among others. All had detailed and clear discussions regarding the Sino-Japanese problem over the years, foreign policy, political propositions, the organization of the past Southwest, Guangxi's position, the actions between July and September of this year, party affairs, civil corps, education, construction, roads, and the newspaper business. Unfortunately, these could not be recorded.

Thoughts Over a Week

In addition to visiting various important figures, I also visited the Provincial Museum, Chengnan Zhongshan Park, the Provincial Second Library, the Military Medical Department's pharmaceutical testing and manufacturing facility, the National Defense Drama Troupe, the Nanning Republic Daily, the Wuming Nanning District Civil Corps Headquarters and its rural construction, and toured Lu Rongting's General's Residence and the Mingxiu Garden operated by Lu, as well as Qifeng Mountain, a famous scenic spot in Wuming. I also strolled through the Nanning city streets at night. In total, this took a week. Looking back on this week, based on personal observations, there are indelible impressions, which I will broadly describe as follows: (1) The educational expenditure of Guangxi Province is greater than any other expenditure, so illiteracy in the entire province has been eradicated. (2) Roads are extremely developed, and the economy has also been developed, so there is no news of bandits or unemployed people. Furthermore, in Nanning City, there are no beggars. (3) Although the government and the people are poor, both above and below have the slogan of "doing things poor," and everything must be done with a tight budget, unwilling to waste a penny. The construction of public utilities mostly adopts the method of conscripting labor and materials to easily complete them. (4) Civil servants, students, and even newspaper reporters all wear military caps and military uniforms, and the value of each set is stipulated not to exceed five yuan. In simplicity, the sluggishness of the past is swept away. (5) Everywhere there are slogans and paintings that awaken the public to love and save the country, and construction goals to save the chaotic, poor, ignorant, and weak. (6) High-ranking officials do not privately own cars. If a car is needed, they request it from the Transportation Department. After use, the car is returned to the Transportation Department. Therefore, everyone has access to a car, but each saves money on car purchases. The above points can be clearly seen by anyone who has set foot in Guangxi, and they are also the most profound impressions on me.

The journey from Yongning still used a Southwest Airlines plane. The one going to Guangzhou was called Beidou. The plane came from Longzhou in the morning. Because the northeast wind was very strong, it was delayed until 12:30 before arriving in Yongning. After refueling, it flew east. Because of the northeast wind, it landed in Guixian for refueling before heading to Rongxian. However, due to the strong northeast wind, the plane was extremely turbulent and the journey was very slow. It arrived in Guangzhou at 5:10 PM. After a brief rest in Guangzhou, I bought a boat ticket north and returned. The journey to Guangdong and Guangxi was thus completed. (The End)

Ministry of Education Distributes to Provinces and Cities: Measures for the Service of Electro-Educational Personnel

On the 28th, the Ministry of Education issued an order to the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, stating that the trainees of the Ministry's Electro-Educational Personnel Training Class are about to complete their training period. Various provinces and cities urgently need to assign these personnel. The "Measures for the Service of Electro-Educational Personnel in Various Provinces and Cities" are hereby formulated for compliance. Furthermore, the "Outline of Service Measures for Radio Guidance Personnel in Education Departments and Bureaus of Various Provinces and Cities," promulgated by the Ministry in September 1935, is no longer applicable and should be abolished. Besides separate orders, a copy of the "Measures for the Service of Electro-Educational Personnel in Various Provinces and Cities" is attached for your department's compliance. This order.

Measures for the Service of Electro-Educational Personnel in Various Provinces and Cities

1. These measures are formulated in accordance with the provisions of Article 3 of the "Measures for the Implementation of Film Education in Various Provinces and Cities" and Article 3 of the "Measures for the Implementation of Broadcasting Education in Various Provinces and Cities" promulgated by the Ministry.

2. Electro-educational personnel as referred to in these measures refer to educational film projectionists, assistants, and broadcasting education instructors.

3. Electro-educational personnel shall be appointed by the education departments and bureaus (or social affairs bureaus) of various provinces and cities. The appointment of educational film projectionists and broadcasting education instructors shall be limited to personnel who have undergone specialized technical training. Personnel qualified by the Ministry's training shall be given priority in appointment. After the appointment of the aforementioned personnel, their name, age, gender, place of origin, education, experience, and treatment should be registered and submitted to the Ministry for record.

4. The duties of an educational film projectionist are as follows: (A) Projection and explanation of educational films; (B) Repair and management of film projection equipment; (C) Custody and delivery of educational films; (D) Assisting in the promotion of broadcasting education. Assistants shall assist the projectionist in performing their duties.

5. The duties of a broadcasting education instructor are as follows: (A) Guiding various radio stations on the installation and repair of radio receivers and their reception methods; (B) Providing the power supply required for direct current generators; (C) Guiding various radio stations to effectively convey the content of broadcasting education to the audience; (D) Examining the results of various radio stations in utilizing educational broadcasts; (E) Assisting in the promotion of film education.

6. At the beginning of each year, educational film projectionists should formulate a projection schedule, averaging the distribution of projection areas and projection dates, in accordance with the provisions of Article 8 of the "Measures for the Implementation of Electro-Education in Various Provinces and Cities," and carry out educational film tours and screenings.

7. After each educational film projectionist completes a screening, they should record the following items in detail and submit them monthly to the competent education department and bureau (or social affairs bureau) for submission to the Ministry for record: Film title, type, number of reels, length, screening location, screening date and time, number of viewers and their educational level, summary of the film's explanation, summary of other lectures, results, and remarks.

8. Educational film projectionists who submit requests to the competent education department and bureau (or social affairs bureau) for the use of educational films from the Ministry are responsible for their safekeeping and should return them within the stipulated return period, without any damage or delay.

9. To facilitate the promotion of their work, broadcasting education instructors may, with the approval of the competent education department and bureau (or social affairs bureau), establish broadcasting education service centers in their guiding areas to handle the installation and repair of equipment, purchase of power supplies, and answer inquiries related to reception.

10. Broadcasting education instructors must inspect and guide various radio stations in their guiding area at least twice each semester and must, within one month after the end of each semester, prepare a report on their work and the general situation of various radio stations and submit it to the competent education department and bureau (or social affairs bureau) for submission to the Ministry for record.

11. The salary and office expenses of electro-educational personnel shall be paid from the education funds of various provinces and cities. Their salary and treatment may be comparable to the treatment of social education personnel with equivalent duties.

12. The detailed rules for the service of electro-educational personnel shall be formulated by the education departments and bureaus (or social affairs bureaus) of various provinces and cities.

13. These measures shall take effect from the date of promulgation by the Ministry of Education.

The Ministry of Education has authorized President Zou of Sun Yat-sen University, and the negotiations have been fruitful.

According to a reporter from the Shanghai News Agency, the exchange of professorial lectures between the Italian Far East and Near East Society and Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou has taken concrete form. When President of Sun Yat-sen University in Guangzhou attended the International University Presidents Conference in Rome this year, he requested the Chinese Embassy in Italy to contact Italy regarding the exchange of one professor. The Italian professor could be designated by China, focusing on mathematics and science. The Ministry of Education has authorized Sun Yat-sen University to contact Italy regarding this exchange. This exchange of professors between China and Italy is the first of its kind, and it is very important for promoting culture between the two countries. Overview of National Education (II)

— Lei Zhen

(Lecture at Employment Counseling Class for Colleges and Above)

(II) Status of National Secondary Education

Lecture 2: The Status of Secondary Education. Secondary education is one level higher than primary education in the education system. Its institutions can be divided into three types: middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools. These three types of schools have equal standards but different characteristics. They are described separately below, starting with middle schools. Middle schools provide foundational training that continues from primary school, aiming to develop young people's physical and mental well-being, cultivate healthy citizens, and serve as a place for preparing for advanced academic studies and various professions. They are divided into junior middle schools and senior middle schools, which can be established together. The duration of study for each is three years. Junior middle schools enroll primary school graduates or students with equivalent academic qualifications. Senior middle schools enroll junior middle school graduates. In areas where the number of junior middle school graduates is too small, students with equivalent academic qualifications may also be enrolled, but their number must not exceed one-fifth of the total enrollment. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there are a total of 1,920 middle schools nationwide, including 493 schools with both senior and junior levels, 41 senior middle schools, and 1,386 junior middle schools. In addition, there are 147 middle school classes attached to other schools, including 11 senior middle school classes and 136 junior middle school classes. There are 415,948 middle school students nationwide, with 10 middle school students per 10,000 people, including 66,325 senior middle school students and 349,623 junior middle school students. Only one out of every three primary school graduates enters junior middle school, and only one out of every five junior middle school graduates enters senior middle school. The reason for the small number of students advancing to higher levels is partly due to economic difficulties and the inability to afford schooling, and partly because there are too few middle schools, leaving no schools to enter. It is evident from the fact that each middle school attracts thousands of applicants, while only dozens or hundreds are admitted. To help students from financially disadvantaged families attend school, the practice of setting up free places in middle schools through scholarship systems should be actively promoted. In addition, new middle schools should be established in appropriate locations to accommodate primary school graduates who cannot continue their education.

Normal schools are places for rigorously training young people's physical and mental well-being and cultivating sound teachers for primary schools. Normal schools that focus on training teachers for rural primary schools are called rural normal schools. In addition, there are four other types: kindergarten normal departments, special normal departments, simple normal schools, and simple rural normal schools. The duration of study at normal schools and rural normal schools is two years, enrolling junior middle school graduates. Kindergarten normal departments are attached to normal schools and are places for cultivating sound teachers for kindergartens. The duration of study is two or three years, enrolling junior middle school graduates. Special normal departments are attached to normal schools or public middle schools. The duration of study is one year, enrolling senior middle school or senior vocational school graduates. Simple normal schools are established to train teachers for compulsory education, with a duration of study of one year for junior middle school graduates and four years for primary school graduates. Those that focus on training teachers for rural compulsory education are called simple rural normal schools, with a duration of study of four years, enrolling primary school graduates. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there are a total of 893 normal schools nationwide, including 151 normal schools, 94 rural normal schools, 389 simple normal schools, and 259 simple rural normal schools. In addition, there are 208 normal departments attached to middle schools and vocational schools (including 115 regular normal departments, 31 rural normal departments, 105 simple normal departments, and 57 simple rural normal departments). The total number of normal school students nationwide is 100,840, with two normal school students per 10,000 people. The ratio of normal school students to primary school students is 1 to 120. There are too few normal school students. To promote universal education, more normal schools should be established and more normal school students should be recruited to cultivate teachers who are physically and mentally sound.

Normal schools are places for training primary school teachers and are very important for primary school education. Therefore, it is stipulated that they should be established by provincial governments or municipalities directly under the Executive Yuan. They may also be established by county governments, municipal governments, or jointly by two or more counties based on local needs. Except for kindergarten normal departments and normal schools that train teachers for primary school crafts, library science, music, home economics, and physical education, private individuals are generally not allowed to establish normal schools. The location of their establishment should be determined based on local conditions and should be set up in cities or villages. They should be established in rural areas as much as possible. Simple normal schools should be established by counties and cities in principle and should be established in rural areas as much as possible. Because there are many rural areas in our country, and the primary schools that have already been established are mostly located in cities, we should promote the establishment of more rural primary schools. Therefore, there is a great need for rural primary school teachers, so we must prepare early and establish more rural normal schools to train rural primary school teachers and personnel for agricultural extension, rural autonomy, economic construction, and local health.

Furthermore, in order to ensure that primary school teachers are evenly distributed throughout the country, the educational administrative organs of each province may divide the province into several normal school districts based on the conditions of the province. Each normal school district may have one normal school and one girls' normal school to cultivate sound primary school teachers for the district.

With the exception of private normal schools, tuition fees are generally waived. Some also waive part or all of the board and lodging fees. Graduates are generally required to serve in the education field and are not allowed to pursue further studies or change to other professions within the prescribed period. Otherwise, they will be required to refund the tuition, board, and lodging fees.

Vocational schools are places for cultivating young people's knowledge of life and skills of production. They are divided into junior vocational schools and senior vocational schools. Those that combine junior and senior levels are called vocational schools. Junior vocational schools enroll primary school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications aged 12 to 18. The duration of study is one to three years, and may be shortened as appropriate when necessary. Senior vocational schools enroll junior middle school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications aged 15 to 22. The duration of study is three years, unless otherwise stipulated by law. Those that enroll primary school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications aged 11 to 20 have a duration of study of five or six years. The establishment of vocational schools should be based on single departments. For example, in agriculture, there are departments such as animal husbandry, sericulture, and horticulture. A vocational school can be established independently for one of these departments, such as animal husbandry or horticulture. By doing so, the scope of the profession is smaller, and the tools needed within that professional scope can be easily and fully equipped. It is also easier to hire specialized talents as teachers and technicians, and what students learn is not just theoretical knowledge, but real skills that can be used to manufacture domestic products and solve livelihood problems. Vocational schools that are established with a single department or subject are called junior or senior vocational schools of a certain department. Those that establish two or more departments are called junior or senior vocational schools of a certain type, such as agricultural, industrial, commercial, or home economics vocational schools. Those that combine several industries are called junior or senior vocational schools. In addition, there is a system of short-term vocational training classes, which aims to train technicians in a certain business. They can be called vocational training institutes, vocational training centers, or vocational lecture halls. There are two types of classes, one for junior middle school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications, and one for senior middle school graduates or those with equivalent qualifications. The training period is set for three to fifteen months, depending on the nature of the profession.

Vocational schools are established by provinces or cities directly under the Executive Yuan, but may be established by local governments or jointly by two or more counties based on local needs. Private individuals or organizations may also establish vocational schools. In the 29th year of the Republic (1940), the central government allocated 890,000 yuan and 950,000 yuan to prepare for the establishment of national model vocational schools, and 300,000 yuan to subsidize excellent public and private vocational schools to encourage them. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 10th year of the Republic (1921), there are 312 vocational schools nationwide, including 42 schools with both senior and junior levels, 74 senior schools, and 196 junior schools. In addition, there are 117 vocational departments attached to other schools, including 77 senior departments and 40 junior departments. There are a total of 41,532 vocational school students nationwide, including 15,254 senior students and 17,178 junior students. There is less than one vocational school student per 10,000 people, and the ratio compared to middle school students is 1 to 10. The number is really too small.

Based on the statistics of the number of students in the above three types of schools—middle schools, normal schools, and vocational schools—there are 10 middle school students, 2 normal school students, and less than 1 vocational school student per 10,000 people. This is, of course, because there are fewer normal schools and vocational schools than middle schools. According to the Ministry of Education's regulations on the standard for the distribution of secondary education funds in each province and city, middle schools account for 40%, normal schools account for 25%, and vocational schools account for 35%. The establishment of normal schools and vocational schools should be promoted. However, the general public has been influenced by the traditional concept that "scholars are the first of the four classes," and they despise farmers, workers, and merchants. Even primary school teachers are considered to be scholars who have failed to achieve prominence. Therefore, most people send their children to middle schools and are unwilling to send them to vocational schools or normal schools. Many young people also think this way. If a child is intelligent and comes from a good family, they should continue their basic scientific training from primary school to middle school, with the expectation of entering a university or specialized school. However, if they want to change to a career, they should observe their personality and see if they are suitable for learning normal school or other professions, and then have them apply to normal schools or vocational schools. It is more useful for them to become primary school teachers or engage in production after graduation, rather than forcing them to pursue further studies, achieving nothing, and finding it difficult to find a suitable job. This is a point of view that is worth paying attention to.

(III) Status of National Higher Education

Lecture 2: The Status of Higher Education. In the education system, education that is one level higher than secondary education is called higher education. Higher education institutions can be broadly divided into four types: specialized schools, universities, independent colleges, and university graduate schools.

Specialized schools aim to teach applied sciences and train technicians. They enroll senior middle school graduates or those with equivalent academic qualifications. The duration of study is two or three years, which may be determined separately by each school according to its type. Medical specialized schools require one year of internship after completing three years of coursework. According to the Ministry of Education's statistics for the 22nd year of the Republic (1933), there are a total of 21 specialized schools nationwide, including 5 national schools, 5 ministry-run schools, 11 provincial schools, municipal schools, and 9 private schools. In terms of the nature of their departments, 12 schools have medical departments, 18 schools have arts departments (literature, law, commerce, education). There are 9 more arts departments than practical departments. In detail, there are 7 art specialized schools, pharmaceutical specialized schools, Fengyi specialized schools, 4 physical education specialized schools, 2 industrial specialized schools, 2 commercial specialized schools, and 1 specialized school each for merchant marine, police officers, water conservancy engineering, teacher training, sinology, and library science. There are a total of 4,511 students in specialized schools nationwide, including 2,363 in public schools and 2,148 in private schools. Compared to public and private schools, the number of students is almost the same, but there are 12 more public schools. (To be continued)

The Construction Drawings of the Ping City Public Sports Field are Decided

Construction to Begin Next Spring

(Special Dispatch from Beiping) The Ping City Public Sports Field has recently been implementing plans for all construction. The field map has now been decided. The shape of the building is a circular track and field field with two central gates. The straight track is 100 meters and the thin track is 200 meters. The command platform is on the west side. Outside the track and field field on the east and west sides, there are four tennis courts, two basketball courts, a baseball field, and a football field. The map has been drawn three times and is very detailed. Yesterday at noon, Li Zhoujiao, the physical education supervisor of the Social Affairs Bureau, Ku Ji, Yuan Dunli, and engineer Yang Tingzhi examined the detailed drawings of the sports field at the Jieying Fancai Restaurant, discussing all aspects of each part. The Department has also completed the work and instructed the engineer to draw detailed sectional drawings. The Yue Nei will be submitted to the Social Affairs Bureau, Qin De, and Ran Chengwei Zheyuan for approval. After approval, the construction fee will be allocated and deposited into the bank. Due to the cold weather, it is not advisable to start construction, so it will be postponed until next spring. However, bidding will be invited within the year. It is rumored in Ping City that the construction cost has been changed to 100,000 yuan. According to reporters' inquiries from various parties, it is said that the construction of the stands of the track and field field will require 140,000 yuan, the running track and jumping pit will cost 15,000 yuan, and the remaining 15,000 yuan will be used to repair the ball field and as a fund. The difference between 100,000 yuan is too great. Engineer Yang Tingbin took a car to Beijing last night to meet with Guan Songsheng to discuss all the field maps and other matters in detail.

In another report, the problem of building the public sports field has been largely decided after the drawings were revised twice. It was previously reported that the municipal government planned to allocate 100,000 yuan in advance and start construction. Yesterday, Li Zhou, a physical education supervisor of the Social Affairs Bureau, told reporters that the municipal government's allocation of 100,000 yuan for construction has been approved today (28th) and the Finance Bureau has been ordered to issue it quickly. However, since the amount is too far from the original budget, I intend to plan with all parties. I am currently discussing methods with the members and I am confident that a solution can be found in the short term. (Jin) October 28th

Recent Overview of Soviet Sports (Continued)

— Song Ruhai

Soviet Russian physical education instructors are divided into four levels according to their level of education. In the spring of 1926, the central government specially established training courses to recruit fourth-level instructors to improve their physical education theory and sports skills. A total of 7,600 people joined the training. The two physical education academies in Moscow and Leningrad established special classes to improve the level of first-level physical education instructors, with more than 1,000 participants. Currently, the education authorities feel that the instructors produced by schools at all levels are not enough to allocate, so it is decided to increase (A) four physical education academies in the autumn of 1936, recruiting 8,000 students, (B) six secondary schools, recruiting 5,000 students, and (C) opening short-term physical education training courses in various villages. Judging from the scale of the above schools, the Soviet Union's training of sports talents is meticulous. According to Ruhai's investigation in various countries, the change in the number of service personnel in the Soviet sports world is more than in any other country.

Since Soviet-German sports are so developed, the cost of common education and construction and the consumption of sports equipment are worth studying. In 1935, the government promoted a total of 500 million rubles for sports. (Each ruble is equivalent to one yuan and three jiao in national currency.) The sports expenditure during the Tsarist era was only 80,000 rubles. In 1936, the government had spent 100 million on the construction of sports fields in various places, and the total value of sports equipment sold by various factories was 318 million rubles. Judging from these figures, the popularity and effectiveness of Soviet social sports are truly advancing by leaps and bounds. There are two largest sports organization in the country, one named Dyname and the other named Spartak. These two associations promote sports and have trained many people with special skills. The Dyname Sports Association has a sports equipment manufacturing plant, and its products currently account for 60% of the entire Russia. All the annual surplus profit is used to promote sports.

Observing the above facts, we know the reason why its sports development is rapid and widespread. There are two points to pay attention to. The first point is that the Stakhanorite movement was at its peak in 1936. The movement increased the economic capacity of workers and civilians and created social prosperity, making the development of sports more popular. The second point is that in 1936, the Central Sports Commission issued more than 6 million medals. It also shows that the effectiveness of social sports is progressing very rapidly. However, the Soviet Union has set the following slogans for promoting sports:

(1) Exercise the physique every year to prepare for labor service and national defense.

(2) To make every young person intelligent and powerful, and to create healthy citizens.

(3) Increase national sports skills and work efficiency.

(4) Special respect and sincerity should be paid to the health of workers.

(Written by Song Ruhai in Moscow, 1936, 7, 5.)

Honoring Birthdays with Local Products - Order to Stop

Collecting Gifts and Sending Them Back with Letters - Participating Businesses Jointly Send Telegrams of Congratulations

Various organizations, including the Shanghai China Native Products Promotion Association, previously initiated a campaign to collect local product gifts to present to Chairman Chiang in Nanjing to celebrate his birthday. Yesterday morning, they received an order from the Second Department of the Military Affairs Commission Office, relayed from Chairman Chiang, stating that, apart from donating funds to purchase aircraft to be presented to the National Government, all other gifts would not be accepted. Consequently, an emergency meeting was convened yesterday morning to discuss the disposal of the collected birthday gifts. The outcome was a decision to return each company's products with a letter, as Chairman Chiang had already stated they would not be accepted. At the same time, a joint telegram of congratulations was sent to Chairman Chiang in the name of the participating native product birthday celebration organizations and businesses. The telegram read: "To Chairman Chiang, Nanjing Military Affairs Commission: Your leadership in the revolution and construction of China serves as a pillar in the torrent, turning the tide from collapse. You unified the country, pacified internal troubles, sought the revival of the nation, and laid the foundation for lasting stability. Your virtues are widely praised, and both domestic and foreign communities admire you. Concerned for the nation amidst the ravages of war and the people in turmoil, you should develop the economy and strive for construction to alleviate the people's hardships and enrich their lives. Your call to lead the National Economic Construction Movement has resonated throughout the country. Our association and others, deeply appreciating your intention for economic construction, and recognizing that the primary lifeline of our nation's economy lies in the rural areas, and that developing the rural economy requires first maintaining our nation's native product production to resist the import of foreign goods and circulate rural finance, have spared no effort in researching and experimenting with the production and marketing of native products over the years. Therefore, we took advantage of your birthday to collect famous native products and improved products from across the country, including clothing, food, and daily necessities, and sent representatives to present them, expressing our sincere wishes. Just as we were about to depart, we received your order that, apart from donating funds to purchase aircraft to be presented to the National Government, all other gifts would not be accepted. Our association and others, complying with your order to cease the gift presentation, respectfully send this telegram of heartfelt congratulations, wishing you health and longevity. From the China Native Products Promotion Association, the Chinese People's Livelihood Education Society, the Shanghai West People's Livelihood Education Experimental Zone, the Shanghai County Party Headquarters, the Gaoqiao Rural Improvement Association, the Zhuanqiao Rural Improvement Association, the February 2nd Movement Promotion Association, the Rural News Agency, Deda Hat Shop, Fujian Store, Yangzhou Sanhe Pickled Vegetables Factory, China National Goods Company, Shanghai Native Cloth Store, Sino-American Xiang Embroidery Shop, Gaoqiao Improvement Zone, Zhuanqiao Improvement Association, Songheyuan, Tongqiao Improvement Association, Zhaoxia Farm, Zhang Shi, February 2nd Movement Promotion, Shanghai West People's Livelihood Education Experimental Zone, and other businesses and organizations."

Memorial Meeting for Mr. Huang Keqiang - Party Department Approves Arrangements

To be Held on November 2nd

This month's 31st is the anniversary of Mr. Huang Keqiang's death. As it coincides with Chairman Chiang's 50th birthday celebration, with flags being raised everywhere, a clash is inevitable. The Central Committee has specially telegraphed all local party departments to move the memorial to November 2nd and combine it with the weekly memorial service for the late Premier Sun Yat-sen. The City Party Department has issued instructions regarding the memorial arrangements, which were approved by the Executive Committee yesterday. Committee member Mr. Chen Junyi has been appointed as the chairman of the assembly. The arrangements are recorded as follows: (1) Convene a Shanghai City all-circles representatives' assembly to hold the 20th anniversary memorial service for the late martyr Mr. Huang Keqiang. (2) Venue: City Party Department Auditorium. (3) Time: 9:00 AM, November 2nd (to be held jointly with the weekly memorial service). (4) Assembly Chairman: To be appointed by the City Executive Committee. (5) Request major newspapers in the city to write articles commemorating Mr. Huang Keqiang for publication in the November 2nd newspapers. (6) Notify all district party departments to instruct their subordinates to send representatives to participate. (7) Starting from November 1st, publish a notice in the newspapers for two days, informing all circles to lower flags to half-mast in mourning. All organs, groups, and schools in the city can send representatives with letters to participate.

Grain Merchants P petitioned the Municipal Government Yesterday to Revoke the Prohibition Orders of Jiangsu and Zhejiang Provinces, and Proposed Measures for the Domestic Circulation of Rice and Wheat in Shanghai

Since the Zhejiang Provincial Government detained rice boats bound for Shanghai, and the Jiangsu Provincial Government resolved to prohibit the export of grain, the Shanghai Grain Trade Association, after an emergency meeting, sent Mr. Chen Ziyi, Mr. Zhu Zixiang, and Mr. , with a petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government to see Mayor Wu. Secretary-General Yu Hongjun received them on behalf of the Mayor. Regarding the prohibition of grain exports by Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces, which greatly affects the food supply of Shanghai residents, they promised to immediately telegraph both provincial governments to revoke the prohibition orders. Subsequently, they went to the Social Affairs Bureau to petition, where Director Pan Gongzhan received them. Regarding the prohibition of grain exports by Jiangsu Province, they had already telegraphed requesting revocation. As for the detention of rice boats bound for Shanghai by Zhejiang Province, they would immediately telegraph requesting their release. The representatives considered the outcome satisfactory and appointed Mr. Gu Xinyi to go to Nanjing tonight to petition the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan, instructing Zhejiang Province to release the detained rice boats and Jiangsu Province to halt the proposed measures. The details are recorded as follows:

Petition to the Municipal Government

The petition to the Shanghai Municipal Government stated: "We believe that the agricultural production of each province in our country varies from place to place, with supply and demand mutually responding, and surpluses and deficits being adjusted, so as to provide sufficient food for the people and prevent damage to their livelihoods. Therefore, the late Premier Sun Yat-sen had the clear instruction to evenly distribute food, and the Central Government issued a clear order on the domestic circulation of rice and wheat in the 21st year of the Republic (1932). Now, with frequent foreign incursions and national crisis looming, preventing rice and grain from aiding the enemy is not only what the government should do, but also what the people should have in mind. On the 9th of this month, our association drafted temporary measures for the domestic circulation of rice and wheat in this city and submitted them to the Social Affairs Bureau to be forwarded to your office for review and implementation. It seems that precautions have already been taken to prohibit the export of grain abroad, with no worries of omissions. However, in recent days, we have received reports from our colleagues that in Jiaxing, Pinghu, and other places in Zhejiang Province, the detention of rice shipments to Shanghai, regardless of whether they are in bags or in bulk, has occurred several times a day. For those in bags, they are suspected of being exported, and the enforcement is even stricter. However, it is not known that packing rice in bags is to prevent water adulteration and fraud, and in fact, it is also to meet the needs of the Shanghai people's food supply. Since the news of the detention and obstruction of rice shipments in Zhejiang Province spread, grain merchants have suffered losses and are worried about unexpected dangers, and have been shocked. Furthermore, Jiangsu Province, which has always been the richest rice-producing area, as reported yesterday, the provincial government has also resolved to strictly prohibit the export of grain, and the atmosphere in the markets has suddenly become panic-stricken. Shanghai has a population of over three million, and their daily food needs depend on a steady supply from the producing areas to avoid shortages. With Zhejiang and Jiangsu successively imposing prohibitions, the food supply in this city will become a dried-up track. The impact is beyond words. In addition to sending representatives from our association to present everything in person, we dare to briefly describe the harms and petition Your Honor to investigate and quickly consult with the Zhejiang Provincial Government to revoke the prohibition order, and order the immediate release of all rice detained in Jiaxing, Huzhou, and other counties. Also, consult with the Jiangsu Provincial Government to halt the proposed measures, so as to comply with national decrees and maintain the food supply of this city. We are sincerely grateful."

Petition to the Central Government

The Grain Trade Association has appointed Chairman Gu Xinyi as the representative of the grain industry to take advantage of the opportunity to go to Nanjing to present aircraft and congratulate Chiang's birthday, and to petition the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan. Mr. Gu is scheduled to take the Shanghai-Nanjing night express train to Nanjing tonight. The petition to the Ministry of Industry of the Executive Yuan is recorded as follows: "We believe that the agricultural production of each province in our country (the middle part is the same as the petition to the Municipal Government). Our association feels that the situation is critical and dare not remain silent. We have sent Mr. Gu Xinyi to present the petition in person to report the harms. We respectfully request Your Excellency to investigate and quickly order the Zhejiang Provincial Government to revoke the prohibition order, and order the immediate release of all rice detained in Jiaxing, Huzhou, and other counties. Also, order the Jiangsu Provincial Government to halt the proposed measures, so as to comply with national decrees and maintain the food supply of this city. We are sincerely awaiting orders."

Circulation Measures

Attached are the four temporary measures for the domestic circulation of rice and wheat in this city proposed to the Social Affairs Bureau on October 9th: (1) The temporary handling of rice and wheat circulation matters in this city should originally be presided over by Your Bureau. However, grain merchants are scattered in the special districts, and most are concentrated in the Nanshi district, making travel back and forth very inconvenient. Therefore, it is proposed that Your Bureau select committee members to handle the matter jointly with our association. (2) When grain merchants in this city ship rice and wheat, they must fill out an application form with the business name, the shipping date, the quantity, the name of the ship, the destination, and the receiving business, and submit it for approval. After approval, a shipping permit stamped by Your Bureau will be issued. (3) The aforementioned application form should be filled out in duplicate, with one copy kept by our association and one copy submitted to Your Bureau for verification and reference. (4) The applicant should carry the shipping permit to the Jianghai Customs to declare the shipment for release. The customs should not allow transshipment without this shipping permit.

Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange Ordered to Seize Cotton Warehouse Receipts - Silver and Banking Industries Held Joint Meeting Yesterday - Resolved on the Spot to Request the Court to Exempt from Seizure - Exchange Petitioned the Court to State Reasons - Court Agreed to Make Changes, Transactions Can Be Settled Today

The Chinese Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange was ordered by the First Special District Court to provisionally seize cotton warehouse receipts, which is bound to cause difficulties for today's settlement. Chairman Mu Ouchu and Director Wen Lanting were specially sent to petition the court. At the same time, the Silver and Banking Industries Associations held a joint meeting and resolved to request exemption from seizure to facilitate circulation. The details are recorded as follows:

Court Ordered the Exchange to Seize

The Chinese Cotton Exchange recently received an order from the First Special District Court, stating that "because two merchants, A and B, traded more than 100,000 bales of cotton, and B believed that the cotton delivered by A did not meet the standards during the transaction, resulting in unsuccessful negotiations between the two merchants, B filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court." The court then ordered the exchange to provisionally seize A's cotton warehouse receipts for sampling and testing the quality. The exchange found no records of A and B's names and therefore reported the situation to the court. Yesterday morning, the court issued another order, still instructing them to comply with the previous order.

Problems Arise with Today's Settlement

Cotton warehouse receipts in the Chinese Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange are in bearer form and circulate in the market based on the receipts, not the people. If the court order is followed and the receipts are provisionally seized, problems are bound to arise with today's yarn and flower settlement. At the same time, the silver and banking industries have a mortgage relationship, which will also be greatly affected. Therefore, the exchange sent a letter to the Silver and Banking Industries Associations requesting a joint meeting, which unanimously advocated requesting the court to exempt from provisional seizure to facilitate circulation.

Joint Meeting of Silver and Banking Industries

The Silver and Banking Industries Associations held a joint meeting at the Hong Kong Road Banking Club at 3:00 PM yesterday. Executive members Wu Yunzhai, Wu Weiru, Qu Jigang, Wang Boyuan, Hu Xiyan, Zhai Yunqing, Pan Jiufen, Yang J眉mei, Zhang Peishen, Liu Wuqiao, Lu Shuchen, Xu Wenqing, and others from both associations attended. Lin Kanghou, Secretary-General of the Banking Association, was also present. Wu Yunzhai chaired the meeting and read the original letter from the Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange. After that, the discussion began, recognizing that it was indeed difficult to provisionally seize the warehouse receipts. A resolution was passed on the spot to petition the First Special District Court to exempt from seizure to facilitate circulation. The meeting adjourned at 5:00 PM.

Changes Made After the Petition

Mu Ouchu, Director of the Chinese Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange, and Director Wen Lanting went to the First Special District Court at 2:00 PM yesterday to meet with Court President Guo Guan, stating the reasons why it was difficult to provisionally seize the receipts and requesting a reversal of the order. The clerk received them on behalf of the president. They left the court at around 3:00 PM. A reporter from the New Society learned from the exchange last night that the First Special District Court had agreed to make changes to the handling, so there should be no problems with today's exchange settlement.

Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange - Reply to the Ministry of Industry

The Chinese Cotton Yarn and Cloth Exchange replied to the Ministry of Industry, stating: "Regarding the reply matter, we respectfully received your ministry's letter Shangzi No. 48968 and respectfully enclosed a copy of the original letter from the Wuxi County Cotton Textile Industry Association. We respectfully learned that your ministry, in order to conduct a prudent study, convened representatives from the Ministry of Finance's Cotton Industry Control Committee to discuss and add to the discussion, and separately decided on the following four corrective measures: (1) The exchange should order both buyers and sellers to pay the principal evidence money in accordance with the law, and the amount should be paid in accordance with the ratio stipulated in Article 31 of the Exchange Law. The exchange supervisor should strictly supervise, and violators will be punished. (2) The exchange's original fixed-term transaction of yarn and flowers, with a term of six months, should be shortened to four months. Initially, the reduction should be done in two stages, with each stage reducing by one month, as a trial. (3) Regarding the limit on the amount of futures trading: 1. The balance of futures trading for each broker in each month shall be limited to 5,000 pieces of cotton yarn and 20,000 dans of cotton. 2. If the limit is exceeded, from 5,050 to 10,000 pieces of cotton yarn and from 20,100 to 30,000 dans of cotton, in addition to the principal evidence money, cotton should be paid at 10% of the registered price per dan, and cotton yarn should be paid at 5%, which cannot be substituted. In addition, a special evidence money should be added according to the amount of the principal evidence money paid, which also cannot be substituted. 3. If the trading amount of cotton yarn is more than 10,000 pieces, every 5,000 pieces exceeded, and the trading amount of cotton is more than 30,000 dans, every 10,000 dans exceeded, the special evidence money shall be doubled progressively, and it cannot be substituted. (4) Reform and correct the flower and yarn appraisers: 1. Cotton appraisers should be hired who have no relationship with the flower and yarn industries and have studied cotton grading. 2. Cotton yarn appraisers should be hired who have no relationship with the flower and yarn industries and hold a textile technician registration certificate from the Ministry of Industry. The above four measures are generally based on the request of the original petitioner, and the allegations of the original petitioner, regardless of whether they are true or not, should legally give our exchange an opportunity to present a defense, and then your ministry can make a fair decision, which is enough to convince people. If only the one-sided complaint of the original petitioner is used to make a decision, it seems to be inconsistent with the general debate system. It is known that your ministry is fair and impartial in this matter and has no prejudice. However, because the original petitioner attacked our exchange, saying that it was indulgent in excessive speculation and focused on profits, etc., it was moved by these dangerous words, and thus there was this move. But if our exchange's representative had been present to clarify the actual situation at that time, it is deeply believed that there would never be such corrective measures. It can be asserted that this is what our exchange has to explain. Moreover, according to the points for correction claimed by the original petitioner this time, some have already been implemented by our exchange, or there are no clear regulations in the current laws and regulations, so it is not convenient to change them rashly. As for the remaining one or two sections, from the surface, it seems that speculators can be more cautious, but in reality, it not only fails to curb the activities of speculators, but also prevents legitimate flower and yarn merchants from hedging, losing the effectiveness of smoothing capital. The business and financial sectors are both suffering. It is not just the small interests of our exchange. The original petition is quite misunderstood about the business policy and management methods of our exchange, and it is quite ignorant of the original intention of the legislation and the structure of modern economic society. Therefore, although it is verbose and references many sources, the root is still one-sided, and it is difficult to understand the intention. Unfortunately, our exchange did not have the opportunity to present the situation, so the points raised by the original petitioner were adopted, and the three or four corrective measures decided, except for those that our exchange had already implemented, the remaining points are mostly obstructive when considering the facts. Even when proving the current laws, it is difficult to implement them. This matter concerns the prosperity of the national flower and yarn industry and the safety of the national enterprise. It is our responsibility and we dare not remain silent. We are forced to state the facts and respectfully ask you to review and approve the request to consult again with the Ministry of Finance and the Cotton Industry Control Committee, send a letter to inform our exchange to send a representative to attend and present the actual situation, so that under the premise of considering both law and fact, we can find appropriate measures to achieve effective results, which is fair and convenient. Respectfully submitted to Minister of Industry Wu."

Party, Military, and Political Circles in This City - Preparing for Large-Scale Anti-Drug Campaign - Held Preparatory Meeting - Decided on Propaganda Principles

According to Guomin News Agency, since the prohibition of opium and rejection of drugs was set by Chairman Chiang for a fixed period and strictly ordered local military and political organs to implement, considerable results have been seen. The Shanghai City Party Department, Garrison Headquarters, Municipal Public Security Bureau, Anti-Smoking Association, and other organs, considering that the two-year drug prohibition period will soon expire, and from New Year's Day next year, drug users should be sentenced to death, and that there are only more than two months left until the end of the year, and drug users may still exist, there should be expanded propaganda to serve as a warning. Therefore, a Shanghai Anti-Drug Propaganda Preparatory Meeting was held at the Garrison Headquarters. Representatives attending included Dai Lizhen from the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Cai Bubai from the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee, Tong Muwan from the City Party Department, Lu Jingshi and Chen Hanzuo from the Garrison Headquarters. Lu Jingshi chaired the meeting and Zhang Bin served as the recorder. After the rituals were performed, the chairman reported that the two-year drug prohibition would soon expire, and from 1937, drug users should be sentenced to death according to law. However, there are still many drug users in Shanghai, so it is planned to hold an expanded anti-drug campaign in the near future to encourage drug users to quit voluntarily. Then the discussion began: (1) The anti-smoking campaign will start on November 10th and end on the 20th. (2) The Garrison Headquarters will issue a notice to warn drug offenders to quit voluntarily. (3) The propaganda materials will be divided into three types: leaflets, slogans, and books, which will be handled by the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee and the Municipal Public Security Bureau. (4) The distribution of propaganda materials will be handled by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. (5) Broadcasting and lectures will be handled by the City Party Department, which will instruct the Entertainment Association. (6) News propaganda will be handled by the Municipal Public Security Bureau. (7) The estimated cost of printing propaganda materials is 300 yuan, which will be borne jointly by the Municipal Anti-Smoking Committee and the Municipal Public Security Bureau. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.
