Japanese Troops - Active Again Yesterday

According to the Central News Agency, the Japanese troops stationed in Shanghai have recently shown signs of activity. The number of troops stationed seems to have increased. Although it is impossible to ascertain the exact number, it is estimated to be around 5,000. The storage of military supplies is also abundant. Yesterday, Japanese troops in the North Sichuan Road area were still patrolling in groups and crossing into the city. The dispatch of Japanese troops within the various garrisons was very busy, and their intention seems to be to avoid outside estimates of their numbers. Japanese troops have also been seen in the Shanghai West area from time to time, but they come and go without a fixed schedule. Therefore, the Japanese troops in Shanghai have been active since the Japanese soldier Tian Gang was attacked on September 23rd. To date, their active area has expanded compared to before.

Two Communists' Anti-Communist Declaration

Willing to work hard for the rejuvenation of the nation under the banner of the Three Principles of the People.

According to the Central News Agency, the Shanghai Municipal Public Security Bureau, regarding the surrender of communists Ding Weisheng and Sun Mengfu, specially invited members of the press yesterday at 2 PM. During the meeting, Sun and Ding made anti-communist declarations, which are recorded as follows:

(I) Ding Weisheng (also known as Shuai Changshu): Since the "September 18th" Incident until now, for these full five years, China has encountered unprecedented tribulations, and the national crisis has become increasingly profound, causing every Chinese person to awaken and realize that Japan's invasion of China is not accidental, but based on the entire plan of the Tanaka Memorial. Realizing that Japan's invasion of China will not stop, but intends to completely swallow all of China, the armed invasion of Suiyuan and Chahar, naval exercises in South China, widespread smuggling across the country, and continuous consular meetings and military attache meetings, coupled with the Chengdu Incident, the Beihai Incident, and the Hankou and Shanghai Japanese sailor incidents, provide opportunities for imperialist attacks. This proves that Sino-Japanese relations are currently extremely tense, and the Chinese nation is facing a critical moment of life and death. Since the Chinese nation has reached a critical moment of life and death, there is no doubt that the Chinese nation can only strive for survival with the strength of the entire nation, otherwise it will only perish. Therefore, the rejuvenation of the nation has become the sole task of every Chinese person. Since I have determined that the rejuvenation of the nation is the sole task of every Chinese person, internationalist class struggle is bound to be rejected in China. At a critical moment of national crisis, it is right to use a united front to call on the strength of the entire nation to carry out national salvation work, but to use the united front as a beautiful name and actually engage in class struggle, and to use the slogan of resisting the enemy and saving the country while actually carrying out Soviet work, will inevitably eliminate the strength of the nation and destroy the work of rejuvenating the nation, which is a great crime. I personally am willing to abandon the standpoint of communism and stand on the standpoint of the Chinese nation, under the leadership of the National Government of the Three Principles of the People, and work hard for the rejuvenation of the nation. In the past, between the government and the people, there may have been some differences in form regarding the work of rejuvenating the nation. I believe that this is because the government and the people are in different positions. The government has heavy responsibilities, so it cannot but adopt a steady approach, while the people are driven by righteousness and act violently. However, the people are the foundation of resisting the enemy, and the government is the guide of the people. Coordination between the government and the people can generate great strength, but it must be that the government occupies a leading position, and the people show enthusiasm for support in order to coordinate and generate great strength. The government's determination to resist the enemy and actual preparations are something that every Chinese person should pray for. I hope that the government will give more leadership and education to the people in the future, so that the people can deeply understand the government's policies and unite the strength of the people under the leadership of the government to complete the task of national rejuvenation. I firmly believe that only when the strength of the people is united under the leadership of the government can the task of national rejuvenation be completed. Many Chinese people are still living in a drunken dream. The government should work harder to awaken them and use them for the government. As for preparatory work, it is extremely important. Without preparation, there is absolutely no way to talk about resistance. With the people, with preparation, and with the leadership of the government, resistance has a chance of victory, and the foundation of national rejuvenation can be laid.

(II) Sun Mengfu: I was born at an inauspicious time, in this era of turmoil. In terms of my personal ability and purpose, I am only suitable to be a scholar, quietly exploring to seek the truth. If it were in a society of peace and academic competition, I would have a little something to offer. Unfortunately, I am in this environment, the country is in great difficulty, and misfortunes gather. Especially the September 18th Incident greatly stimulated me, so I was taken in by heresies and mistakenly entered the Communist Party. Afterwards, I knew that it was not suitable for me, but under coercion, I could not extricate myself. Soon I was arrested and imprisoned. In prison, after much pain and reflection, I deeply repented and vowed never to participate in political activities again, and to concentrate on scientific research. Then, even in the current environment, I may be able to achieve something and be of some benefit to the country and society. After being released from prison, I tried my best to abide by this oath and hoped to realize it. However, in the political aspect, I was only passive, unable to grasp the correct center, and unconsciously still retained the poison of the past. Therefore, I was arrested again this time. Now, after clear guidance and a long period of reflection, I feel even more the mistake of blind action in the past, and the lack of thoroughness in avoiding any political relations and not seeking correct leadership. Communism is originally not suitable for a quasi-colonial country like China, and theories such as class struggle are even more sufficient to weaken our own strength and invite foreign troubles in our country. I had already abandoned such fallacies, and now I also see through the roots of the so-called "united front" and "national defense government" various slogans of surface resistance. They are truly a transformation of communist theory, used to agitate the people and usurp orthodoxy. In terms of the current situation, resisting the enemy and saving the country is certainly the first priority, but it must be under the leadership of the government, and only by concentrating national strength can it be effective. Otherwise, there will be division and disintegration, and internal collapse first. How can we resist the enemy? Since the National Revolution, our country has advanced to a country of the Three Principles of the People. Following this correct path, we can develop upward, eliminate all internal and external troubles, and reach a truly free and equal realm. As for other political doctrines and schools, they are all harmful and useless to our country. This can be proven not only in theory, but also verified in fact. Now that I have vowed to reform and start anew, from now on I will do my best under the banner of the Three Principles of the People, be loyal to the party and the country. My sincerity is limited and cannot be fully expressed. I only hope that in future actions, I can show more.

Lin Kanghou Sponsors the China-Siam Association, Lin Responds in a Letter, Willing to be Listed as a Founding Member, Publishes the Articles of Association Draft

The Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission of the Central Government, in order to promote friendly relations between China and Siam, initiated the organization of the China-Siam Association. Yesterday, it sent a letter to Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce and Deputy Head of the Siam Inspection Group, to solicit his participation as a founding member. Lin replied in a letter agreeing. The reporter of the Industrial Society explored the letters between the two parties and the draft of the Association's purpose and articles of association as follows:

Soliciting Founding Members

The China-Siam Association sent a letter to Lin Kanghou yesterday to solicit his participation as a founding member. The original letter stated, "Mr. Kanghou, with respect, this Association aims to promote Sino-Siamese culture and develop Sino-Siamese economy. Therefore, we are organizing the 'China-Siam Association' in China and the 'Siam-China Association' in Siam, communicating with each other to strive for greater friendship between the people of the two countries. However, this matter is of great importance and must rely on collective wisdom and effort to succeed. We have long admired your concern and enthusiasm, and dare to borrow your esteemed name as a founding member. If you grant your support, it would be a great honor. We respectfully wish you good fortune. Sincerely, the Preparatory Committee of the China-Siam Association."

Reply Agreeing

After receiving the letter, Lin Kanghou replied yesterday, expressing his agreement. The original letter stated, "In reply, I have just received your letter soliciting my name to be listed as a founding member of the China-Siam Association. I strongly agree and approve to have my name listed as a joint founder. Correspondingly, I reply to your association, hoping that you will check and take note. Sincerely, Lin Kanghou, Chairman of the National Federation of Commerce, to the Preparatory Committee of the China-Siam Association."

Association's Purpose

China and Siam are both located in the Far East. Geographically, they are neighboring countries, and in terms of bloodlines, they are also mixed. Today's Chinese and Siamese people cannot be distinguished due to centuries of intermarriage. As for the close economic relations and shared international interests, they are also well-known facts. Loving neighbors and being kind to neighbors are famous sayings of Chinese sages and have been regarded as national policies throughout the dynasties. Coexistence and co-prosperity are also China's only foreign policy. In recent years, Siam's diplomacy has also focused on peace and sought coordination. Therefore, China and Siam have the same voice and should strive for further close relations. This should be understood by enlightened people in both countries. We have initiated the China-Siam Association based on this purpose to promote the communication of culture, the development of economy, and the continued increase of national sentiments between the two countries. However, this matter is of great importance and must rely on the support of everyone. Therefore, we are making an appeal and widely soliciting comrades. We hope that great gentlemen will actively participate and jointly accomplish this great cause. Then, it will not only be our good fortune. Sincerely, the Founders of the China-Siam Association.

Draft Articles of Association

Draft Articles of Association of the China-Siam Association: Article 1. This association is named the China-Siam Association. Article 2. The temporary general meeting address of this association is located at the Overseas Chinese Affairs Commission in Nanjing. Article 3. This association aims to promote Sino-Siamese culture, develop Sino-Siamese economy, and connect the feelings of the Chinese and Siamese people. Article 4. Anyone who agrees with the purpose of this association and is introduced by one of the founders of this association or two members may become a member of this association. Article 5. Members of this association shall pay an annual membership fee of six yuan, but those who donate one hundred yuan in one lump sum may become permanent members. Article 6. This association shall have eleven directors to carry out the affairs of this association. Article 7. The directors shall be elected by the general meeting of members of this association for a term of one year and may be re-elected. Article 8. This association shall have one chairman and one vice-chairman of the board, who shall be elected by the directors from among themselves for a term of one year and may be re-elected. Article 9. The chairman of the board shall manage all the affairs of the association. If he leaves office due to circumstances, the vice-chairman shall act as his agent. Article 10. This association shall have a general affairs section and a publicity section, each with one section chief, appointed by the chairman of the board, to be responsible for the matters under their respective jurisdictions. Article 11. The board of directors shall hold a regular meeting every three months. If there are important matters, the chairman of the board may convene an extraordinary meeting. Article 12. This association shall have one honorary president and several honorary vice-presidents, all of whom shall be elected and appointed by the general meeting of members. Article 13. A general meeting of members shall be held every year in September. The date shall be notified by the chairman of the board two months in advance. If there are special circumstances, the chairman of the board may convene a meeting at a fixed time upon the request of seven directors or one-half of the members. Article 14. These articles of association may be added, deleted, or amended by a majority vote of the members present at the general meeting of members.

Electric Lights in the Six Leitang River South of the County Lighted Up Yesterday

The electrical business in Puxi, Shanghai County, is undertaken by the Xingshi and Zhenshi Electricity Companies. The area is divided by the Zhuanqiao Six Leitang River. The north of the river belongs to Xingshi, and the south belongs to Zhenshi. Both are supplied with electricity by the Huashang Electricity Company. The areas north of the river were connected to electricity last year. The areas south of the river, Beiqiao, Minhang, Yutang, etc., have also been connected to electricity. The Zhuanqiao area has not been connected due to engineering reasons. Zhuanqiao is the second largest town in Puxi, and industry and commerce are quite developed, so electricity is very much needed. Residents and merchants have repeatedly sent letters to the Zhenshi Company, requesting prompt power supply. Qiao Nianchun, the manager of Zhenshi, has already signed a contract with the Huashang Electricity Company and obtained approval from the Municipal Public Works Bureau. The power was connected yesterday, so it was brightly lit. All electricity on the Shanghai-Kang Road from Wujia Lane south to the Huangpu River was temporarily stopped from 2:00 PM to 3:00 PM yesterday.

Zhang Zuming's Appeal Case Against Zhou Jinggeng et al. Was Judged Yesterday, Gao Yushu et al.'s Perjury Not Accepted, Zhang's Incidental Civil Appeal Rejected

Zhou Jinggeng, the former comprador of the Xue Mailuo Accounting Firm at No. 9 Edward Road in the French Concession, sent his partners Gao Yushu, Feng Ti, and Wan Guirong on the afternoon of June 9, 1934, to the China Industrial Bank to withdraw 18,000 yuan in cash back to the firm. Not long after, a thief broke in and robbed 12,000 yuan. He reported to the French Police, and the detectives arrested suspects Zhang Zuming, Zhuang Jimeng, Zai Lianyou, and Tang Qingyue and sent them to the Second Special Court for public prosecution. After trial, it was found that there was no solid evidence of crime by Zhang, Zhuang, Zai, and Tang, and they were acquitted. The case was appealed to the Higher Third Branch and the Supreme Court, and the three trials concluded with the original judgment being upheld. Later, Zhang Zuming hired a lawyer to file a lawsuit in the criminal division of the Second Special Court against Zhou Jinggeng, Gao Yushu, Feng Ti, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, Wang Guirong, etc., for perjury and false accusation, and incidentally filed a civil suit, seeking compensation for damages of 50,000 yuan. After trial, the court ruled that Zhou Jinggeng and the other six were not guilty, and the incidental civil suit was rejected. Zhang Zuming was not satisfied with the original judgment and filed an appeal with the Higher Third Branch. The Higher Court opened a collegial panel a few days ago to summon both parties for trial and announced the end of the debate, awaiting the scheduled official judgment. This has been reported in the newspapers. Yesterday afternoon was the date of the judgment. Neither the appellant nor the appellees nor their lawyers reported. At 3:30 PM, Criminal Division Chief Wu Tingqi and Assessors Liao and Wang went to the Criminal Third Court to deliver the judgment. The main text stated, "The original judgment is revoked with respect to the parts concerning Gao Yushu, Feng Ti, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, and Wang Guirong. The continuous perjury of Gao Yushu, Feng Ti, Wan Guirong, Qian Genghua, and Wang Guirong is not accepted. The rest of the appeal is rejected." Also, Zhang Zuming's incidental civil appeal is rejected.

The Trunk Murder Case Was Concluded Yesterday, Lin Gendi Examined and Found No Mental Illness, Mao A'gen et al. Still Insist on Being Framed, Court Orders Judgment on the Fifth of Next Month

In the headless trunk murder case, during the last court session, the defense lawyers Fan Gang and Shen Xiaoxiang for the defendants Mao A'gen and Jiang Yuantan requested that the blood on the floorboards and the blood stains left on the rattan box used to hold the corpse be determined to be of the same type, and that Lin Gendi be examined for mental illness. Therefore, the hearing was postponed. The First Special Court has now sent the case to the Institute of Forensic Medicine for examination. The results showed that Lin Gendi did not have any mental illness, and whether the blood on the floorboards and the blood on the rattan box were of the same type could not be determined because of the long time and the lime.

Yesterday afternoon, this case was continued by Judge Zhong Qing of the First Special Court and Prosecutor Zhang Zongru. Police Lawyer Zhang Shizhu stated that, during the postponement, Ye Kuiyu, the manager of the Cunfu Lane house at a certain number, was re-summoned by the police. According to Ye, on the afternoon of August 3rd of this year, two women went to Cunfu Lane to rent a house, but they thought the rent of over 30 yuan was too expensive and did not rent it. They also went to a certain number one, but the rent of 25 yuan was not agreed upon. The two women were about twenty years old, five feet three inches tall, with short hair, wearing

Black and blue cheongsams

with white trim. The other was about twenty years old, five feet two inches tall, and seemed to have a Ningbo accent. They had considered renting the pavilion room at number two. According to Ye, it was not rented to them. Now Ye is also in court, please question him. Then Ye Kuiyu submitted a report on the previous situation. The court asked whether the number two of Cunfu Lane had been rented out. Ye answered that it had not been rented out. If he was lying, he would willingly be punished. Then Hua Detective Huang Fosen submitted a report on the investigation of Ye Kuiyu. The court immediately questioned Lin Gendi, who provided, the deceased was determined to be Cai Ying, killed by Jiang Yuanying when Mao was also at the scene, the date was August 9th at 2 PM, I

Actually didn't do it

etc. Mao A'gen said that this was a slander by Lin. On August 9th, I and the firefighters from certain numbers competed in volleyball with the firemen from a few different numbers, and after the game, we had dinner, and I never left the fire station. Jiang Yuanying also insisted that he was framed. The court, considering the facts clear, ordered the opening of debate. Then, Police Lawyer Zhang started by saying,

This case was solved

because someone reported it, not because the police arrested them on their own initiative. Lin Gendi unintentionally mentioned it to someone at the cigarette shop on Carter Road on September 2nd, which led to the solution. If Lin intended to frame someone, he could have reported it to the police. Moreover, the examination showed that Lin had no mental illness, and his testimony was consistent from beginning to end, without any confusion. Jiang Yuanta first admitted it, according to his confession, the reason for killing Cai Ying was due to jealousy and love rivalry. And they all confessed during the on-site inspection in court, so

Criminal facts

are very clear and should be judged according to law. Fan Gang and Shen Xiaoxiang then argued for the defendants, regarding this case, until now, it is still unknown who the murderer is. Although according to Lin Gendi's confession, the deceased was Cai Ying, who lived at number 10 of Cunfu Lane, the investigation showed that there was no Cai Ying in number two of that lane. The date of the murder Lin originally said was August 8th, but after the police investigation it showed that Mao A'gen was at the fire station all day on that day, so it was changed to August 8th. Moreover, one of the female attendants of the Yangzhou troupe of the Daxin Company

Named Zhu Fenglan

and not Cai Ying. Furthermore, Lin Gendi's confessions were contradictory and none were credible and should be announced innocent. The court then gave the forensic report on the autopsy by Zhang Yan of the First Special Court to the lawyers of both parties to read. It was said that the corpse changed particularly slowly when the body lost all of its blood and its moisture decreased. The time for the corpse to decompose could last up to eighteen hours, so the deceased was about fifty hours after death when she was examined. The court then designated Fan Lawyer to be Lin Gendi's

Defense under

Zhang Prosecutor's opinion, said that during the autopsy, it was found that the head and legs were cut very smoothly, and those who were not accustomed to knife and axe work could not have such skills. Now, the defendants Mao and Jiang in this case were firefighters, and their daily work involved the use of axes, so the situation was consistent. Lin Gendi's confession was consistent, and Jiang Yuantan initially admitted it in court. Moreover, the police checked the axe used by the defendants, so his confession should be adopted. Now that there is a crime scene and evidence in this case, it should be considered that there is evidence and a judgment should be made according to law. Judge Zhong then announced the end of the debate, and set the sentence to be announced at 10 AM on the 5th of next month.

Meal money of four corners

General accounting office

was not just once

and that his colleagues Ying Lingeng.

Wang Jie-gui, was also cooperating, so Ying and Wang were arrested in succession. Forgery of Bank of Communications Notes: Fu Yi Accused of Conspiracy; Fu Consistently Denies Forgery, Claiming Purchase from Guangdong; Court to Announce Verdict Tomorrow

Guangdong native Fu Yi, accused of removing the bank name and train emblem from eighteen one-yuan banknotes of the Bank of Communications, then scorching the areas around the removals and exchanging them for new notes at the bank. Recently, many instances have been discovered on the market of using waste paper from other provinces to patch up the bank name and train emblem of Bank of Communications notes, passing them off as genuine notes. As a result, the General Inspectorate of the Police Department instructed detectives Kang Zengxiang and Sun Jishan to arrest Fu. A search of Fu's residence uncovered tens of thousands of Guangdong Provincial Bank notes (already unusable). He was brought before the First Special District Court. Fu consistently denied forging the Bank of Communications notes with waste paper from other provinces. The court adjourned the hearing for further investigation. Details have already been reported in this newspaper. Yesterday morning, Judge Feng Shide conducted a further hearing in the criminal court. First, Sun Jiasheng, an employee of the Shenyi Money Exchange on Jiangxi Road, testified that Fu usually traded in public bonds and bought Guangdong Provincial Bank notes. At the end of last month, Fu had received 9,000 yuan in Guangdong Provincial Bank notes from the exchange, bringing the total received to around 40,000 yuan. Subsequently, Xu Yuanlai, an employee of the Issuing Department of the Bank of Communications, testified that two years ago, the Kao Zhen Preserved Meat Shop at 688 North Sichuan Road had exchanged one-yuan banknotes of the bank with the train emblem and bank name burned out. At the time, the intention behind the removal was unknown, so the police were notified to investigate, but there were no leads. It was only after the discovery of forged notes on the market that the reason became clear, leading to Fu's arrest when he came to exchange notes. Questioned, Fu Yi stated that he had purchased these Bank of Communications one-yuan notes in Guangdong two years ago and denied any forgery. He hired lawyer Fan Gang to defend him. After an exchange between police lawyer Li Zhishan and lawyer Fan, Judge Feng declared the hearing closed, scheduling the verdict for this Saturday.

Japanese Chamber of Commerce: Unable to Proceed

Due to Opposition from Chinese People

A Central News Agency report states that recently, rumors have spread in Shanghai that Japanese merchants are actively preparing to revive the Chamber of Commerce, attempting to disrupt China's financial system. According to a journalist's inquiry to relevant parties, Japanese merchants Uda Goro and others established a Chamber of Commerce in Shanghai during the sixth and seventh years of the Republic (1917-1918), which later profited greatly before being suspended. For nearly a decade, Japanese businesses in Shanghai have not been performing as well as before. Some Japanese merchants, seeing the potential for profit in the Chamber of Commerce, approached leaders of the Chinese business community in the city a month ago to discuss the revival of the Chamber of Commerce. However, due to strong opposition from the Chinese people and lack of cooperation, the effort has now been suspended.

Labor Strike at Shanghai West Silk Weaving Factories: Result of Party and Government Mediation

Work Expected to Resume This Morning

A Dagong News Agency report states that workers from six silk weaving factories in Shanghai West—Baohua, Tiancheng, Fuxing, Yucun, Yongfeng, and Yiyou—recently jointly launched an industry union. Tiancheng and Baohua factories dismissed eleven preparatory members, including Lu Shaocheng, causing worker dissatisfaction. A conflict erupted with guards and staff at the Yucun factory, leading to seventeen arrests. Workers at all factories went on strike yesterday, sending representatives to party and government agencies to request assistance. The details are as follows:

Strike Petition

The six silk weaving factories, Baohua and Tiancheng, employ more than 1,200 male and female workers. Because of the launch of the union, Tiancheng factory dismissed four preparatory members, including Lu Shaocheng, Zhang Xianguang, Chen Zaizhu, and Zhu Xiaozhong. Baohua factory also dismissed seven preparatory members, including Xu Housheng, Zhou Xian'e, Zhou Ju'e, Huang Heqin, Zhang Yuezhen, Zhu Shengrong, and Zhang Baixi, eleven in total. This caused outrage among the workers. The afternoon before yesterday, at 5 pm, they went to the Baohua factory to demand reinstatement, but to no avail. Passing by the Yucun factory, workers there heard the call and rushed out to respond, leading to a clash with guards and staff at the Yucun factory, with injuries on both sides. The Caojiadu Public Security Bureau arrested seventeen workers. Yesterday morning, workers from all factories gathered in Shanghai West and held a meeting, unanimously deciding to strike and sending sixty representatives, including Xu Longsheng, Chen Rongcan, Wang Jingxiang, and Wang Baisong, to party and government agencies to request assistance. Arriving at the Fenglin Bridge Municipal Party Headquarters around 9 am, they were received by Li Weixiong of the Civil Movement Section, who, after inquiring about the situation, advised the workers to wait quietly for a legal resolution. They then went to the Social Affairs Bureau of the Central District of the city, where they were received by Wang Xianqing, the Mediation Director of the Second Section, who gave a satisfactory response. They dispersed around 1 pm.

Six Demands

After implementing a joint strike, the workers presented six demands at yesterday's general meeting, seeking mediation from party and government agencies: (1) Immediately release the arrested workers, including Zhang Baixi (2) The medical expenses of all injured workers should be borne by the Yucun factory, which is the capitalist side (3) Injured workers should be paid their wages during the injury period (4) Order the capitalists from Baohua and Yiyou factories to withdraw the dismissal orders and allow Zhang Baixi and others to return to work (5) Factory capitalists must guarantee that similar incidents will not occur again in the future (6) If the incident is delayed and cannot be resolved, wages should still be paid during the work stoppage.

Party and Government Mediation

After receiving reports from Baohua and the other six silk factories, the Municipal Party Headquarters and the Social Affairs Bureau determined that the joint strike was highly related to local security and the future of the industry and the workers’ livelihood, so the Municipal Party Headquarters sent Li Weixiong, and the Social Affairs Bureau sent He Jingyuan, to investigate the truth at various factories in Shanghai West. However, because the workers insisted that the arrested workers must be released before further negotiations could take place, the party and government representatives went to the Municipal Public Security Bureau to discuss the issue and decided that the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions would be responsible for bailing out the seventeen arrested workers, including Zhang Baixi. Future issues would be resolved legally. In the afternoon at about 4:00 PM they summoned representatives of the various factory workers to talk, advised about the pros and cons, and advised the workers to resume work first, and the six conditions requested would be settled on a scheduled, lawful basis. Representatives of each of the workers indicated their acceptance, promising to explain to all workers the command to return to work, but because it was late there wasn't enough time to inform all workers of the factory, therefore they could go to the factory and resume work this morning.

Shanghai Customs Notice: Supplementary Import Tariff

Item 632, Section D

The Shanghai Customs, in order to implement the supplementary regulations on tax collection for Item 632, Section D, of the import tariff, issues Joint Notice No. 1551, stating: "Now, according to the order of the Ministry of Finance, the following supplementary provisions should be made for Item 632 (Buttons), Section D, of the import tariff: 'Buttons plated with precious metals should be classified under the button tariff (Section D). The import duty to be levied should not be lower than the tariff rate for the button tariff (Section A).'" The above measures will be implemented from November 1st, 1936. Merchants are required to comply accordingly. This notice is hereby issued. Supervisor Zhu Changnian, Customs Commissioner Ba Runsen.

Detectives Disguised as Merchants: Nine Notorious Thieves Arrested; Firearms and Stolen Goods Confiscated; All Thieves Detained for Further Interrogation

Between September 9th and October 21st, two residences at 17, Lane 53, Ruijin Road, and 10, Lane 366, Tangshan Road, were invaded by large gangs of notorious thieves who used firearms to intimidate and silence the occupants, stealing valuables worth several hundred yuan before fleeing without a trace. Reports were filed with the police for investigation and arrest. Around 7 am the day before yesterday, Shao Jingfan, a Chinese detective at the Jiaxing Road Police Station, learned that the bandits involved in these two cases were meeting at Room 11 in the Xizang Hotel at 10 Yu Qiaqing Road to plot the theft of a large sum of money from a certain residence. He collaborated with detectives Yang Xinzheng and Chen Lusheng, secretly booking Room 16 and disguising themselves as merchants to observe the situation. The gang of thieves had not yet returned. Detective Shao and Detective Black Deng from the Western District waited on the street. At 3 pm, they saw a large group of thieves entering the hotel one after another. Without making a sound, they continued to wait. After a while, the ringleaders, Wang Laoshan and Zhang Shaokang, both from Shaoxing, and their accomplices Cheng Yuan and Zhang Xianggen, staggered in. They were immediately arrested. A White Langlin pistol and sixteen bullets were found on Wang Laoshan and Zhang Shaokang. In Room 31, they found five more people: Lin Zhongfa from Ningbo, Sun Yonglin from Hangzhou, Chen Bingde and Wang Guiyuan from Shaoxing, and a woman from Hangzhou named Zhao Ji. Zhao Ji's waistband held a white satin ribbon, which was identified as stolen property by the victim of the Tangshan Road robbery. It had been given to her by Sun Yonglin. They also went to the Kangti Road No. 410 pawn shop in the French Concession and retrieved a stolen watch, which was brought to the police station along with the others for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Bureau of Public Works, detailed the case and requested an extension for further investigation. Detective Shao then explained the process of arresting the defendants, presenting the seized guns and watch ribbon. Judge Zhong Qing questioned the nine men and women, and ordered them to be detained for further investigation.

Bao Gang Case Reopened: Continued Interrogation of Witnesses; Zhang Qinghong's Wife Summoned to Court; States That Yang Yuehua Once Lived in Her Home

The case of lawyer Bao Gang, accused by Cui Changgui, a chauffeur from the Special Affairs Group of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, of seducing his fiancée Yang Yuehua, hiding her in the home of Zhang Qinghong, the chief of the Third District of Chuansha, and instigating a divorce, has been prosecuted by the District Court, with Bao Gang and his tea attendant Zhang Xinkui accused of being intermediaries. The District Court has repeatedly ordered further investigation. The Commissioner of the Jiangsu Supervisory Office also dispatched a special investigator to review the case. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Xie of the District Court continued the hearing. Bao Gang claimed illness and did not appear. Zhang Xinkui was brought from detention for questioning. First, witness Zhang Yao, a 31-year-old resident of Xiaowan, Chuansha, was questioned. "Zhang Qinghong is my husband. Bao Gang, my husband's classmate, brought a woman, Yang Yuehua, to stay for one or two weeks. Bao left after bringing her. Yang Yuehua came to Shanghai three or four days later and then again for two days. My husband and I were together. Yang's husband came looking for her. The official showed a photo and asked if the person in the male attire was me and the person in the female attire was Yang Yuehua. According to Bao, she was Bao's concubine. I called her 'Mrs. Bao' out of politeness and didn't press further. Later, as we became closer, I also called her 'Sister-in-law.' Bao Gang didn't come often, but he would come to my husband if he needed something. Yang Yuehua lived next door. This is the truth." After making a sworn statement, she was asked if she had ever seen Bao's wife. She replied that she had not. Then, witness Fang Wanru and others were questioned. Fang stated that he/she was a room attendant at the Fang Gui Hotel and did not remember anything about opening rooms for (…). He/She also did not pay close attention to Yang Yuehua's appearance. As for Room 322 on May 11th, he/she heard that it was opened by someone surnamed Zhou. He/She also said that the room was managed by the conductor Zhou Ming (?). Then, Yang Yuehua, 21 years old, from Pinghu, formerly residing at Jiezhufang, Penglai Road, currently residing at Fumin Road, testified that she went to Bao's house on May 10th after arguing with her husband, and went to the Grand Eastern Hotel on May 11th. However, she did not remember whether it was Room 321 or Room 332. She did not recognize the two tea attendants, and had not opened a room since then. However, for three days, the 13th, 14th, and 15th, Zhang Xinkui called her three times to go to Bao's place, but she did not want to go. Asked, "Since you didn't want to go, how did you go with him?" She answered evasively and said that she went to Zhang Qinghong's place in Chuansha on the 19th for over a month and was far away from the district. She pointed to Yao and identified her as Zhang Qinghong's wife, who called her "Sister-in-law." Later she went to Shanghai, staying at the Jiangsu Reception Hall and then Nantian. Bao smoked opium and did not get up in the morning. Zhang Xinkui was his confidant. Then, Cui Changgui testified, "Since my wife disappeared, I have been burning incense and praying to the gods. Later, my wife's friend Zhang Jinhua told me, and I understood the situation. Please investigate," etc. Then, Zhang Xinkui testified in court, still claiming that he was being framed. The official adjourned the hearing for further questioning, and Zhang Xinkui was returned to detention.

Strange Tale of a Farmer's Wife Giving Birth to Five Puppies

Abandoned in the River; Is It Evil?

Tao Laowei, a 38-year-old farmer living in Dongcahejing Town, Shanghai West, married the younger sister of Ye Yuxiang from the Qianjia Ancestral Hall ten years ago. The couple's relationship is good, but they have no children. This summer, Ye suddenly became pregnant. Tao Laowei was eager to have a child and was overjoyed. Recently, Ye's abdomen became very large, and she was about to give birth. Tao asked his neighbor, an old woman named Yu Chen, to come to his house to assist with the delivery. However, around 9 pm the night before last, she suddenly gave birth to five puppies, which soon died. Fortunately, the mother is doing well. Soon, the news spread to the surrounding area, and people flocked to see the puppies. Tao Laowei feared that the mother would be startled, so he denied the story. That night, he threw the nine puppies into the Cahejing River.

Liu Huizhi and Others Found Not Guilty of Breach of Trust and Embezzlement; Case Delayed for Two Years with Multiple Judge Changes; Court Finally Delivered Verdict Yesterday

Shareholders Zhang Chongfu and He Jiechun of the China Industrial Bank accused manager Liu Huizhi and permanent director Li Liao Zhi of the bank of breach of trust and embezzlement in a private prosecution to the First Special District Court. The court consolidated the cases because the allegations made by the plaintiffs were largely the same. Liu argued that the allegations were untrue and filed a counterclaim against He Jiechun, Weng Pengnian, Zhu Ruping, Yan Yuquan, and others, requesting that the plaintiffs be prosecuted for false accusations. Recently, Yi was transferred to Anhui Province, and Judge Fu Lin continued the proceedings. After summoning evidence and witnesses, the court held several hearings and concluded the case. The verdict was announced yesterday afternoon, stating: "Liu Huizhi and Li Liao Zhi are both not guilty. The court has no jurisdiction over the part of the private prosecution concerning rent. He Jiechun, Weng Pengnian, Zhu Ruping, and Yan Xiaoquan are all not guilty. The plaintiff's related civil suit is dismissed."

Chinese Industrial Bank Held Creditors' Meeting Yesterday

Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Meditates Reconciliation: Resolved to Petition the Court for Instructions

Since the China Industrial Bank suspended operations in October 1934, although the court declared liquidation and bankruptcy, no solution has been reached for more than a year. Recently, Lu Jingxing and others, in accordance with the law, requested the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to mediate reconciliation and submitted a reconciliation plan. The Chamber held a creditors' meeting in the auditorium yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM. Because creditors had differing opinions, the meeting was quite chaotic. It was decided to submit the voting results to the court for review. The details are as follows:

Meeting Situation

At 2:00 PM, creditors arrived one after another and signed in. First, Ke Ganchen, a standing committee member of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, announced that more than three-quarters of the creditors were present, so the meeting could be convened in accordance with the law. He reported that Lu Jingxing and others, partners of the China Industrial Bank, had requested the Chamber to mediate reconciliation based on the registered claims of Lu Xihou, the transferee of the China Industrial Bank, who was bankrupt. Accountant Xi Yushu reported on the review of the accounts at the office of bankruptcy administrator Xu Yongzuo. After the reconciliation plan was read, the creditors rose to speak one after another. The main points can be divided into (1) questioning the Chamber's legal basis for mediating reconciliation, (2) what capacity do Lu Jingxing, Tu Bao Yi, and Ji Zong (?) request reconciliation, and has their personal property been audited, and (3) although past attempts at reconciliation had failed to return any deposits, they supported reconciliation by the Chamber, and (4) the previous proposal to return 20% of the deposits, while the current reconciliation plan only returns ten percent, which is illegal and should be opposed. Each held to their reasons, and the scene became chaotic.

Vote

Chairman Ke Ganchen explained that the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce was completely neutral and that creditors could vote to support or oppose the reconciliation. If two-thirds of the votes supported reconciliation in accordance with the bankruptcy law, then the remaining one-quarter would be bound by it. If three-quarters supported ordinary reconciliation, then the creditors could still pursue litigation and would not be bound by it. However, the above decisions would still need to be presented to the First Special District Court for explanation before proceeding. The creditors then voted, and three representatives were publicly elected to verify the votes on the stage. To ensure accuracy, the vote was handed over to accountant Xi Yushu for detailed review. After explaining to the creditors, Chairman Ke Ganchen announced the adjournment.

Reconciliation Plan

The reconciliation plan proposed by Lu Jingxing, Tu Qi Yi, and Li Zong Sui is as follows: (1) All debts of the China Industrial Bank, based on the registered amount in the bankruptcy proceedings of the China Industrial Bank and Lu Xihou, will be borne by Lu Jingxing and others, who will raise 10% of the outstanding debt (i.e., 10%) in cash within 30 days from the date of reconciliation, as settlement of the responsibilities of Lu Xihou, Lu Jingxing, Li Zong Sui, and Tu Bin Yi. (2) The cash will be borne by Liu Chunpu, Jin Yangtian, Chen Shizhen, and others. (3) Three representatives elected by the creditors will, together with Lu Jingxing and others, liquidate, collect, and dispose of the assets of the China Industrial Bank and Lu Xihou. After deducting necessary expenses, if there is a surplus after paying the 10%, the surplus will be distributed proportionally to the creditors, but only up to a total of 20% (including the first 10%). If there is any further surplus, it will be enjoyed by Lu Xihou and has nothing to do with the creditors. (4) This reconciliation releases Lu Xihou, Lu Jingxing, Ji Zong Sui, and Tu Bin Yi from responsibility, but the creditors still have the right to seek compensation for the amount not received from other responsible persons of the China Industrial Bank. To preserve the rights of the creditors, they may entrust their representatives to exercise the right of subrogation and may file lawsuits or non-litigation actions in the name of the bank, Lu Xihou, or the creditors' representatives.

Tofu Industry Commemorates the King of Huainan Yesterday

The Qiaojiazhai Shanghai Tofu Industry Association held a celebration yesterday in commemoration of their industry ancestor, King Liu An of Huainan. The event was unprecedented in its grandeur. The details are summarized below:

Celebrating the Industry Ancestor

Yesterday, the Shanghai Tofu Industry Association, located at 18 Qiaojiazhai, held a celebration in commemoration of the anniversary of the death of their industry ancestor, King Liu An of Huainan. Beginning at 9 am, more than 200 industry members, including Wei Jinsheng, Zhang Fugen, Han Wenjun, Qiu Senlin, and Ni Fengxiang, attended. In the afternoon, a Western-style religious ceremony was held, and in the evening, industry members gathered for a meal to celebrate the occasion solemnly.

Anecdotes about Liu An

King Liu An of Huainan, whose surname was Liu and given name was An, was a native of Huainan who lived during the Later Han dynasty. He was the 18th generation descendant of Emperor Gaozu Liu Bang. His father, Zhi, had only one son. When the King of Huainan was fourteen years old, his mother's teeth deteriorated due to old age, making it difficult for her to eat hard foods. Sometimes, she could not find suitable food to swallow. The King of Huainan was extremely filial. Seeing this, he worked hard to research soft foods to help his mother eat. Soon, he unintentionally invented tofu, which has been passed down to this day. There are more than 700 families in this city who make a living from the tofu industry.

Western Police Prevent Firefighting: Shantytown Representatives Petition

Request Thorough Investigation and Permission to Build; Municipal Federation Agrees to Forward to Bureau of Public Works

A.E.G. Celebrates Longevity for Shou Linwen

Electrical engineer Shou Linwen has been working at A.E.G. China Electrical Factory for 25 years. On the 30th of this month, the factory's Shanghai office, under the order of the German headquarters, held a celebration for Shou. A banquet was held at the New Asia Hotel. Shou is amiable and highly valued by the factory. In 1909, Shou was sent to the German headquarters for a five-year internship, mainly in factories producing steam turbines, generators, switches, motors, sheds, and electric meters. Finally, he briefly interned in more than ten other manufacturing plants one by one. He returned to China during the outbreak of the European War, and the representative in China was repatriated. Therefore, Shou was put in charge of the affairs in China. At that time, there were several steam turbine generators that had been sold but not yet installed. Shou alone took on the completion and installation. He is a rare talent in electrical engineering.

Letter

To whom it may concern: I have just read a news item in your newspaper's news column on the 29th of this month, stating that the Municipal Party Headquarters is preparing to celebrate Chairman Chiang's birthday, and that a recreational gathering will be held at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, etc. It is true that there was a proposal to hold a recreational gathering to celebrate Chairman Chiang's birthday, but due to the Central Government's order to suspend birthday celebrations during this period of national crisis, the recreational gathering scheduled for the evening at the Municipal Chamber of Commerce has been cancelled, except for a party members' meal. I hereby inform you of this and hope you will check and correct it. Sincerely, Shanghai Special Municipal Executive Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, October 29.

To whom it may concern: In today's edition of the local news on the 28th, there is a report on the case of lawyer Bao Gang being accused of seduction. It states that Zhang Qinghong, the chief of Chuansha District, was instructed to ask the county magistrate to investigate, and that deceiving me is deceiving the Control Yuan and deceiving the Party is being a reactionary element. This is not consistent with the wording of the interrogation at the time. Zhang, as a public official, should abide by the law, and even if he wants to deceive me, he cannot deceive the Control Yuan. If he deceives the Party, he will be an unfaithful element. I said that even if there is no instruction to the county to investigate, the office can order the county to thoroughly investigate, etc. Please correct this immediately to avoid misunderstandings. Sincerely, Wu Zhang, Secretary of the Jiangsu Control Commissioner's Office, October 28.

Commercial News

Yarn and Fabric Sales Sluggish; Yarn Market Price Increase Also Flattens; Many Bulls Cutting Losses

The yarn market rose in the afternoon after a morning decline, and the situation is still calm. As the price has fallen for several consecutive days, the number is already considerable, and it should be able to stabilize. However, the demand for yarn is still sluggish, so people's hearts are scattered. One merchant has already cut half of his large position. Most people do not see much upside in yarn in the near term. The price of Osaka Sanpin yarn for the near month is 16-17 yuan higher than the distant month.

Tendered Yarn Drops Near Term, Rises Far Term

The tendered yarn market opened in the morning. Because of poor sales of yarn, people's confidence was weakened, and the price continued to fall by 1.5 yuan. The distant month, however, rose by 0.7-0.8 yuan to 1 yuan. In the first session, the near month rose again by 1.7 yuan, and the distant month returned by 0.5-0.6 yuan. By the time of the third closing, it was heard that yarn sales were still thin, and many floating buyers cut their losses. The market declined. As a result, the November price was 1.4 yuan lower than the previous day's closing price, and the distant month was 0.4-0.7 yuan lower. The market opened slightly lower in the afternoon by 0.1 yuan in the near month, but the distant month turned firm. The second session rose again due to rising raw cotton prices. The third closing heard that yarn transactions were lacking, and the momentum was stable. As a result, each month rose by 0.3, 0.5, 0.8, 0.9 yuan to 1.3 yuan compared to the morning closing price. It was found that Hengyi sold 2,900 bales, Tongji 800 bales, Mingde 1,800 bales, Changyu 2,800 bales, Huamao 2,900 bales, Fengtai 5,750 bales, Renfeng 800 bales, Yichang 1,000 bales, Dachang 1,500 bales. Cotton Price Decline Stabilizes Slightly

The cotton market rose in the afternoon after a morning decline. This is because foreign cotton is weak, demand for real cotton is not strong, and old, coarse cotton is still stuck in November and December. However, compared to the high price on the 21st, it has already fallen sharply by 3.7-0.8 yuan. It may temporarily stabilize. In the afternoon, there were rumors that there were still problems with the delivery of October cotton. People's confidence was restored. In fact, the degree of decline was too severe, so a rebound is possible.

Tendered Cotton Falls in Morning, Recovers in Afternoon

The tendered cotton market opened in the morning. As the decline was violent the previous day, the momentum stabilized slightly. Prices recovered by 0.1-0.3 yuan in each month. The first session turned soft, and the third session fell again. Because one merchant drastically cut their long positions and went short, the market became loose. By the time of closing, the distant month had fallen sharply by 0.35 yuan. The situation was very bad. As a result, each month fell by 0.25-0.4 yuan compared to the previous day's closing price. The market opened suddenly nervous in the afternoon. Each month fell sharply by 0.3-0.4 yuan. The second session suddenly fell by 0.2-0.3 yuan. By the third closing, it had recovered again. As a result, each month recovered by 0.3, 0.4, 0.5 yuan compared to the morning closing price. American Cotton Merchants Awaiting Election Results; Cotton Prices Weaken Again by Closing

Yesterday, the American cotton market opened. The Liverpool news was not good. Colleagues and foreign merchants bought, short positions covered, and each month rose by 1-3 points. There was less short selling. Cooperatives bought the December position at a limit price. Weekly weather reports were favorable for the harvesting of new cotton. Actual demand was active, and the basis for high-grade cotton was very firm. New buyers were normal. Everyone was waiting for the election results. Cooperative short selling increased, and market prices weakened again. The spot price fell by 4 points, and futures fell by 4-7 points. British cotton spot prices rose by 12 points, and futures rose by 3-5 points. Indian cotton initially rose due to large purchases by European exporters, but then fell back as long positions were liquidated. Pingguoer rose by 1.6-1.75 rupees, Aomula rose by 0.25-1.5 rupees, and Bairoxi rose by 1.5 rupees. Original telegram left (28th telegram).

Piece Goods, Cotton Cloth Market Difficult to Sustain; Various Places Telegraphing to Stop Shipping; Transactions Suddenly Become Desolate

Yesterday, the cloth market continued to soften due to the continued softening of the yarn and cotton market. Cloth factories were not worried about the scarcity of yarn and thread, and the selling price became cheaper every day. The customer groups that were recently selling well, such as Changsha, Hankou, Jiujiang, Wuhu, Yunnan, Fujian, Guangdong, and other regions, have recently become cheaper in Shanghai, and there is no confirmed market price. Because the true situation is difficult to understand, all goods have fallen unanimously. People's hearts are very empty, and all customer groups have telegraphed and sent letters, all saying that local market prices have fallen, adding to the goods, and asking them to stop loading, or sell them in Shanghai. Therefore, the market is quiet and the market is difficult to sustain. Yesterday, 16-pound coarse cloth hand goods were competing to sell off. Zhentai Factory's Hongfu brand, Baoxing Factory's Baoxing brand, Shenxin Factory's Ren Zhong brand, as well as Saima, Gengyu, and Bianlong brands, all fell (per piece) by 1.3 yuan or so. However, Yihua Factory's various grades of coarse cloth still maintained the original price. Eastern goods fine cloth continued to fall (per piece) by about 0.1 yuan. Shanghai cloth, 84 original cloth, also fell (per piece) by 0.05 yuan. The transaction was very desolate. Only fine twill was still stable because of good demand. Colored goods, real tribute, flannel, broadcloth, printed flannel, and other goods also slightly fell (per yard) by 0.0025-0.005 yuan. Natural color twill flannel and white lining flannel are extremely scarce on the market, and the allocation of goods is not strong, so the market is quite firm.

Yuanfang Piece Goods Rebound Also Starts

Yesterday was the date of the 3,012th auction by Yuanfang Foreign Firm, displaying five types of goods: Western satin, Yuan velvet, tribute flannel, Yuan silk, and foreign red cloth, totaling 49 brands in 99 boxes. The market was stagnant for customer groups because the previous period was suspended due to the situation. In the following two periods, the customer goods were rushed to be installed, and the industry competed to buy, and the auction price rose too much. Customer groups watched and did not move forward, and the market on this street faded. The bidding price rose twice before and is now falling. There is no trend that will not fall. According to the industry's vision, it will be difficult to improve in the next period. Of the seven brands of Western satin auctioned, Three Heroes Lion Monkey was 0.04 yuan higher per yard, and the rest were 0.01-0.02 yuan lower. Yuan velvet Five Flower Cave rose 0.03 yuan, and Jiufang West Chess fell 0.02-0.03 yuan. Tribute flannel was 0.0075 yuan lower, and Yuan silk Andian Bao Cai Bashi fell 3.8 yuan to 4 yuan per piece, Eighteen Sons Luanfeng Five Stars fell 2.7 yuan to 3.3 yuan, Huazhu Zhulin Renqiu fell 2 yuan, and merchants Quanfu Eighteen Scholars Bozi Kuali were about 1 yuan lower. Only the sea cow temper price was flat, and the rest fell 0.4-1 yuan. Yanghong cloth was priced at 5 pounds and was a light-weight item, with only one box. The industry competed to buy, and the price was still good.

Flourishing Trade in Fine Eyebrow and Pearl Tea

Yesterday, both the foreign firms and the local firms trading in Ping-Shui green tea saw continued brisk business. The Jardine Matheson, Concord, and Jardine Skinner & Co. foreign firms had not yet met their order quotas from overseas, so they continued to purchase over a thousand more chests. Among the local firms, the most traded were the mid-grade Fine Eyebrow and top-grade Pearl Tea, while the most popular Ping-Shui tea was the Mei Cha Qu Wei. Prices remained generally consistent with the past few days, but the trading houses are still suffering losses and remain pessimistic.

Finance Commodity Speculation: Supply and Demand Discrepancies

The gold market continued to weaken yesterday due to sluggish demand for downstream pure gold, falling another six dimes. However, due to inconsistencies between supply and demand after the decline, the market fluctuated. The final result was extremely uncertain. In the early morning, overseas silver markets showed London rising and the US remaining flat. Major players claimed that after the market closed, prices would be quoted with an additional 0.0625, and there was strong demand from India with limited sellers. The forward silver price in Monterey rose between five and one-tenth of a cent. Exchange rates opened higher but contracted. The London spot gold price fell one penny. The Central Bank announced its rates, with both London and New York remaining flat. The customs gold unit shrank by one cent. The standard commodity speculation price was listed at $1,156.10, but the opening price in the morning was slightly higher. After the opening, sellers began to be slightly more active. The HSBC announced its rates, with both London and New York remaining flat, gradually trending downward. The silver balance announcement showed a one-cent increase. Buyers in Yong maintained and rebounded. In the middle of the day, the market remained uncertain, with those eager to sell at a high price continuing to flood the market, coupled with fluctuating sentiment. By noon, the market had turned weak again. Subsequent market fluctuations were more pronounced, and the situation struggled to stabilize. Major players experienced inconsistencies between supply and demand. Indian silver initially rose by five annas, then receded by one anna in the second instance, ultimately remaining stable. Swap rates trended firmer, with buyers offering a premium of slightly over three yuan. The following details the market situation for the day:

The morning opening price was $1,155.20, up one dime from the previous close. Cheung, Ku Tai, Heng Hing, Yuan, and Shen Kang actively sold, retreating to $4.10. The HSBC announced its rates, with both London and New York remaining flat and then flat again. Fook Hing and Wing once advanced to $4.50. Tai Tak Shing and Yuan Mao Wing sold again at $4.00. The silver balance tax announcement showed a one-cent increase. Tai Tak Shing, Chip Fung, Wing, Yuan Heng seized the opportunity to buy, rebounding to $5.00. Fook Yu Yat, Tai Tak Shing sold at $4.50. Chip Fung, Wing, and retail investors advanced to $5.10. Yu Hsin Cheung Yat, Tai Tak Shing sold again, falling to $4.20. Fook Hing, Wing, Heng Yu still acquired. The noon closing price was $1,154.30.

The afternoon market opened at $1,154.40. Fook Tai Heng purchased futures, rising from $4.30 to $4.70. Man Hing Heng Yu sold, retreating to $4.30. Yuan Tai, Chip Fung, Wing, Yat, Tai Tak Shing acquired futures, rising to $4.70. Yuan Liau Wing sold. Gan Cheung Cheung and others also supplied, retreating to $4.40. Chip Fung, Wing still acquired. The closing price was $1,154.50.

The closing price was based on the Central Bank's commodity speculation standard price, lowered to $1,156.10. Based on the closing price, the conversion rate was about one yuan. The November futures price was $1,152, and the December price was $1,154. The morning premium was $1,150. The red gold price was $1,161.20. The spot market was stable. Refined red gold was sold by Tai Kang Run to the Hankow syndicate for 140 taels at a premium of $13, sold at a premium of $8. Tianjin goods were sold at a premium of $11.25, but there were few buyers. Swap transactions were scarce. The premium for short positions had risen to over three yuan, but there were few takers.

Trading within the market was dominated by Chip Fung, Wing, Yuan Heng, Yuan Wing, Fook Fung, Wing, and Fook Tai Heng due to their financial strength. Chung, Ku Tai, Ying Fung Heng, Wei Wing, Cheung Fung, Heng Yu, Sheng Yuan Wing, Man Hing, Shen Tai Wing, and others occupied

Based on the day's market situation, the market was generally weak, opening at $1,155.20 and closing at $1,154.50. The highest price was $1,155.10, and the lowest price was $1,154. There was a fluctuation of $1.20. Compared to the previous close, the market fell by six dimes. There were 1,282 November futures contracts remaining, held by five long positions and twelve short positions. December futures contracts totaled 6,293, held by twenty-six long positions and eighteen short positions. The total number of transactions was 875 in the morning session and 707 in the afternoon session.

Foreign Exchange: Mostly Exchange Transactions Yesterday—London and New York Remained Flat

The foreign exchange market experienced fluctuations yesterday due to interbank exchange transactions. In the early morning, overseas telegrams showed that London's spot and forward rates both rose by 0.1875. The New York silver market remained unchanged. The forward silver price in Monterey rose between five and one-tenth of a cent. The London spot gold price fell one penny. The British pound rose against the US dollar by 0.0125, and the US dollar shrank against the British pound by 0.0125. The British pound remained unchanged against the French franc, and the US dollar rose against the French franc by 0.0115. The Central Bank announced its rates, with both London and New York remaining flat. The customs gold unit shrank by two cents. The foreign exchange market opened in the morning with the near-term selling price for the British pound at 1 shilling, 2 and 46875/100000 pence and a half penny against the US dollar, and the US dollar at $29.50 and $0.5625 against the British pound, which meant that both London and New York remained flat compared to the previous close. After the opening, banks engaged in mutual transactions. The HSBC announced its rates, with both London and New York remaining flat. Subsequently, the silver balance tax announcement showed a one-cent increase. Japanese banks conducted Japanese-US dollar exchange transactions with the Dalian syndicate, while foreign banks conducted British-US dollar exchange transactions. As a result, the market remained calm. Chinese merchants sold US dollars, and banks bought them. The noon closing price remained calm. In the afternoon, banks still had a strong appetite for transactions. Traders from Hong Kong sold British pound positions. The overall trend fluctuated. The Indian silver rate finally squeezed past the long position by four annas, and there were no changes in the end. The closing selling price for the British pound was 1 shilling, 2 and 46875/100000 pence and a half penny against the US dollar, and the US dollar at $29.50 and $0.5625 against the British pound. Compared to the previous close, both London and New York remained flat. Chinese merchants slightly increased their holdings of US dollars. The following is a record of the transactions:

The British pound opened in the morning with the near-term selling price at 1 shilling, 2 and 46875/100000 pence and a half penny against the US dollar. Great Britain and Citibank sold December futures at 0.4375 to Macgregor, and Chinese merchants sold October futures at a half penny to Yau Lee. In the afternoon, HSBC and Great Britain purchased October futures at a half penny. Hong Kong sold spot futures to Citibank and Macgregor at a half penny. The closing selling price for spot futures was 1 shilling, 2 and 46875/100000 pence and a half penny against the US dollar. November futures were 0.4375, December futures were 0.375 and 0.40625 against the US dollar, and January futures were 0.3125 and 0.375 against the US dollar. The purchase price was slightly higher.

The US dollar opened in the morning with the near-term selling price at $29.50 and $0.5625 against the British pound. Zhejiang and Macgregor purchased November futures at 0.5 yuan, at a rate of 3 to 2.8606. Shanghai purchased November futures at 0.5 yuan. Citibank purchased December futures at 0.4375. Securities: October Government Bond Delivery Completed

Yesterday, the 29th, was the delivery date for October futures at the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange. The total amount delivered was $17,715,000. Of this amount, $12,955,000 was settled directly by the brokers through account transfers, and only $4,780,000 was delivered through the exchange. The majority of the deliveries were made by retail investors. Although the market situation experienced multiple shocks and constant changes in the environment, the market price fluctuations were limited. The difference between the highest and lowest prices for Class B and Class C bonds was less than $5, and the difference for Class A bonds was only $3.60. Considering the facts, there were unfortunate events in Chengdu, Beihai, Hankou, and Shanghai. Before September 6th, the Guangxi incident was still very tense. The bond market was stimulated by these events, and prices fell sharply but also rose quickly. Because the Guangxi incident was resolved on September 7th, and the Sino-Japanese incident went through several rounds of negotiations, with the situation fluctuating between tension and relaxation, the bond market trended towards fluctuation. Therefore, on October 26th, the last day, compared to August 26th, the first day, the market prices for Class A and Class D bonds were equal, and the market prices for Class B and Class C bonds were slightly lower by approximately $2. Class E bonds were slightly lower by approximately $1.25. The difference in market prices was $1-2, reflecting the different choices made by investors. Grains: High Grain Prices in the North; Flour Speculators Active; Prices Up by 3-4 Cents in Each Month

Yesterday, the flour market opened in the morning and prices for each month showed signs of a sharp increase. Although the quoted price for foreign wheat fell by one dime, speculators were not swayed. Even though there were rumors about foreign wheat, they were difficult to confirm. Therefore, after the opening price, buyers were very active again. Prices for each month were two cents better than the previous day. After the second round of trading, transactions were very active. Due to the expulsion of many speculators, the market showed some weakness. By the afternoon opening, the market was initially calm, but then, due to the fact that grain prices in the north had not eased and were even higher than those in Shanghai in some places, speculators took advantage of the situation and absorbed supplies aggressively. Prices for each month rose by another two or three cents. Observing the subsequent trend, if foreign wheat consistently failed to approach, speculators inside and outside the industry would inevitably be eager to move, it was said.

Spot Prices Remain Firm and High; 期麦 Remains Difficult to Ease

Yesterday's 期麦 market saw prices for each month gradually rise in the morning opening. Although the quoted price for foreign wheat showed a slight decline, the spot wheat situation remained strong due to tight supplies in the production areas, and transporters were naturally unwilling to let go. Therefore, at the time of the opening price, market sentiment gathered and was two or three cents better than the previous day. By the afternoon opening, because the flour market rose again and spot wheat prices were raised by five cents, the opening price was three or four cents higher than the morning. Transactions in each round were not very active. In the spot wheat market, the price of special-grade wheat was raised by five cents, while medium-grade wheat remained unchanged. Shandong wheat opened at $6.10, medium-grade at $6.07. Mingguang wheat at $6.07, Yanghe wheat at $6.05, Nanjing wheat at $5.83, medium-grade at $5.80, Guangshui wheat at $5.78, medium-grade at $5.70, Jiangbei wheat at $5.90, Chongming wheat at $5.80, medium-grade at $5.75, Hankou car wheat at $5.94, medium-grade at $5.92, Tiantai wheat at $5.91, Gaoyou wheat at $5.88, Dongtai wheat at $5.90. As for Tu Yang Chien, due to the renewed activity in the urban and rural markets, the price was raised by one dime, and Yang Chien rose by one and a half dimes. The price of thick and thin broken japonica rice, which had already fallen, still had no fixed standard. The sales of new Yin Yuan were stagnant, and the price was cut by one to one and a half dimes.

(North Shanghai) Yesterday, about 30 ships arrived from downstream, and the sales of top-grade broken japonica rice and special new japonica rice were sluggish, and the price remained stable. Although the sales market for medium-grade broken japonica rice and new japonica rice was not brisk, the subsequent market was tight by a few cents. The appetite for tea seed rice in this city was flat, the sales of buns were uninterrupted, and the price was peaceful. The price of new and old Yin Yuan rice was short by one dime, the price of Yin Yuan rice fell by more than one dime, and the identity was still soft and there was no way to sell it.

Cantonese Merchants Again Actively Purchase Coarse Indica Rice

Therefore, sentiment improved even further, and the price of high-grade rice rose sharply by one to two dimes, and the customer demand for medium-grade rice was even more active, so it rose sharply by three dimes.
