Soybean Prices Again Affected by Declining Prices of Dalian Soybeans

Yesterday, the soybean trade was not deserted. Tong Market opened with over 7,600 bags of green and yellow soybeans from various sources, which were sold to factories in Fuzhou, Xiamen, Shantou, and this street. However, the market continued to be hit by the devaluation of Dalian soybeans. Yesterday, the oil mills continued to order five cars of Siping Street soybeans for delivery in November at a price of $5.30, which was another dime lower than the forward market. Other soybeans were affected and fell by five cents to one dime. Sesame and foreign wheat remained unchanged, and the overall situation was not optimistic. There were few transactions of spot raw sesame. Yesterday, only over 370 bags of Haozhou sesame were opened at a price of $9.97 and $9.80, it was said.

Sugar Market: Sugarcane Crop Failure; New Sugar Costs Inevitably Rise

Yesterday's sugar market trended flat. The guild's trading panel made no significant changes. For example, #24 coarse granulated white spot was $21.60, with higher grades at $21.70. Transshipment goods were $6.20, and #10 Dutch red, which could arrive on the first of next month, was $6.10. Eastern White #4 (J) mark was $6.45. The #9 spot TM mark was $21.30. The prices for other grades remained unchanged. The Jinxin, Dahua, and Zhenji #1 refined white sugar from local factories were all priced at the original levels. Domestic sugar prices were softening due to weak sales and concerns about the upcoming new crop, so market prices might continue to ease. However, the situation in the production areas was very different from that in Shanghai. It was heard that the sugarcane-producing areas were experiencing insufficient rainfall, leading to poor development and inevitable crop failures. As a result, sugarcane prices were expected to be $4 higher than in previous years, and it was predicted that new sugar prices would be higher than current market prices, making it difficult for prices to fall below current levels. According to reports, the latest production prices, such as Qing劃申, must be raised by $3.90, Upper Huanggang Qing by $13.70, and lower grades were in short supply. For example, Longjiang Qing and Jiazi Qing also required $12.60, Upper Zhiyang $18.50, and other grades varied. Qibai and Fenbai were both out of stock.

North-South Goods: Quanzhou Dried Longan Opens at 5,000 Pieces

Recently, dried longan sales have been brisk, and the market has tightened. Prices in Quanzhou, Xinghua, Tong'an, Zhangzhou, Anhai, and other producing areas have all rebounded. The 5,000 boxes of Quanzhou bubble circle recently arrived from the local businesses have all been cleared yesterday, except for a portion of the consignment goods. The upper grades rose by three or four yuan, and the middle and lower grades also rose by two or three to four yuan. However, the smallest grains did not rise much due to competition from Guangdong goods. According to news from the production areas, prices were higher than those in Shanghai. If sales do not decline in the future, prices may rise again.

Silk and Tea: Overseas Silk Market Remains Stable

Yesterday's overseas silk market saw mixed trends. The New York and Yokohama stock market prices seemed to have risen enough and then retreated. The near-term price in New York fell by 0.015, and the long-term price fell by 0.04. The spot price in Yokohama fell by 15 yuan, and the futures price fell by 10 yuan. However, overseas silk merchants maintained firm prices. For example, yesterday the discussion on the price of 83 and 75 evenness silk from New York, Shanghai silk, and Guangdong silk was generally raised by about 0.02. The price of Japanese silk in Lyon rose by one franc, and the prices of other Chinese silks remained unchanged. From this perspective, overseas market sentiment remains stable. However, compared with the Shanghai market, it is difficult to match. Shanghai has risen rapidly and far beyond overseas markets in recent days. Therefore, yesterday's silk market was inevitably firm, and transactions were very few, it was said.

We Should Emulate Mr. Lu Xun

— Ai Wu

Mr. Lu Xun has passed away. In the fourth item of his will, he wrote, "Forget me, and take care of your own lives." Although this was written specifically to his family, it is also suitable for us. Of course, we will not forget him, but in addition to mourning and commemorating him, we should also learn from him so that we can live our lives well in the future.

I believe that the first thing we should emulate is not his short stories or his essays, but his love for humanity, especially his love for the oppressed and the harmed.

He initially went to Japan to study medicine. He said that his purpose was to "cure the suffering of patients like my father who were." Later, when he engaged in literature, he did not regard literature as the only thing, loving it like a treasure, but only "wanted to use its power to improve society." Therefore, the material for his novels was "mostly taken from the unfortunate people in a morbid society, with the intention of exposing their suffering and drawing attention to treatment." When translating, he also paid special attention to "the works of authors from oppressed nations" because the works of oppressed nations mostly conveyed resistance and calls for help.

I remember Tolstoy saying something like this: "The most valuable thing in the world, the foundation for all missions, is not love for art, but love for humanity. Only those who serve in this way have hope of success." I think this is absolutely right, and Mr. Lu Xun's success is an excellent illustration of this.

The second thing we should emulate is his spirit of struggle.

When Mr. Lu Xun became famous in literature, he appeared in society with the prestige of a warrior. Throughout his life, he resisted feudal society, resisted imperialism, and resisted the forces of darkness, and he never weakened even in his old age. He could have written one or two dozen short stories and one or two dozen novels, but he refused. He would rather write many miscellaneous essays. This was not because he lacked material or energy, but because he saw that "at this time, only struggle and combat are needed." Because he knew that miscellaneous essays could be used as seven shots, as throwing spears, "things that can kill a bloody path together with the reader," unlike novels that "expose the suffering and draw attention to treatment," which is a somewhat detached attitude. Now, looking at his essay works, they are just like his criticism of "Luo Yin's 壙書," "almost all talk of resistance and indignation." From this point, we can see even more that his loyalty to life is far greater than his loyalty to art.

Note: The quoted sentences are all taken from Mr. Lu Xun's posthumous works.

October 22nd.

Meeting in Death

— Tzu Kang

Who would believe that Mr. Lu Xun is dead!

The sky is so cold, people feel like they've been whipped with ice, and ice chains have rolled across their backs. It's not pain, it's coldness. It freezes on one thought: Is this a dream? The cold freezes the thoughts.

And how many young people have suffered this cold whipping!—For a warm stranger in their hearts, a fifty-six-year-old man. Yes, an old man has forged deep friendships with a group of young people. Thousands of small streams are converging on a focus, and old age has not drawn a ditch in the middle of the road.

Perhaps it's not tears that are used to mourn this farewell, but a moment of breath held in the cold whipping, reason and memory grabbed back: This is real!

Isn't it true that in the center of the mourning hall lies at rest that young man who never grew old until his death—his heart was so young, strong, and upward-moving. The work of leading the way is interrupted, he puts down his hand lamp, and quietly slips away from the young people, leaving behind a piece of darkness and thorns. It's so sudden, how much pity is he swallowing.

In the corner, how many familiar and unfamiliar faces from his lifetime cannot restrain their emotions, and are secretly covering their faces, afraid of the silence of death? But they cannot help but raise their red eyes and look again at the face drooping in the flowers.

How many young people, girls, and children sigh:

"He's still so young, no silver beard!"

"He didn't speak, he didn't even say hello, this is the first and last meeting!"

"..."

How many children bowed deeply to this "old grandfather," perhaps they have read the fairy tales translated for them by the "old grandfather," the stories written for them. Under the leadership of the teacher, they pay their final respects, and they will sincerely thank him in their little hearts. Perhaps they are half a century apart, and youth makes them understand this "old grandfather" a little less, but they will have a closer connection to the books he translated.

People who didn't want to leave immediately stayed in the outer room of the mourning hall. There was anxiety, hesitation, and a lingering attachment that was hard to dispel like light smoke. I wanted to hear his voice, even if it was a greeting or a reprimand; I wanted to see his smile—a minute of smile was good too.

But he was deathly quiet, his chest didn't move, not even a cough.

Wreaths and flower baskets were constantly increasing, carefully held in the hands of young people, placed at his head and beside him, so quietly as if afraid to wake him, whispering blessings: Rest well! How many hands offering wreaths were trembling.

How many people hated "death" on this day, because it can snatch away some of the lives that people cherish. "Death" is so cruel and unforgiving, taking away this wave that is occasionally seen in the sea of people—beautiful, powerful, with the majesty of a giant. I can't find this wave again, it sinks into the vast sea, not annihilation, but differentiation, dissolving into new thousands of waves.

Larger waves are growing, using new power to impact, all so strong, so stubborn.

Passionate girls wanted to cry out, turning their heads towards the wall, and suddenly remembered the two big characters "Silence" at the door, turning their rampant passion into solemn grief—Silence, silence will sublimate into power on the leaves.

Lying in front of us is a long road, and the "living" must breathe, walk, and work in the road; the "living" will bravely face the oncoming storms with firm faces and kick away the darkness.

Everyone believes that the "ageless comrade" is continuing to breathe, this pause is rest, he secretly sends off the ranks of the "living," he listens attentively to the struggle between the "living" and the darkness, and smiles and waves to future generations.

"He's just stretching his tired muscles and bones, he's asking for a long vacation, won't you let him rest?" A voice was saying in people's ears.

"Where are his children!" Someone found the seven-year-old boy in a corner, with his father's shadow on his face. The innocent child jumped around his mother and relatives, and did not forget his books and his picture albums. He should be grateful for the education he had received in those seven years.

"Mom! Dad..." The child thought of something and wanted to find his father, his little eyes turned, and he suddenly changed: "Where's Uncle? Where's Mr. Huang?" He knew his dad wouldn't speak again, as if he had sensed the tension in the air, and lowered his little throat as well.

"Death" will not draw a clear outline in a child's heart. There is only strangeness and surprise for this strange thing.

Who would believe that "he" is dead! But everyone was whipped by the cold.

In front is a long road, let's raise the torch that was put down with millions of hands. October 21st.

Crying for Mr. Lu Xun

— Ye Zi

I suffer from tuberculosis and pleurisy,

He wrote to me, sent me a dollar, and said to me:

"Young man, don't worry, rest and recuperate,

The illness will naturally get better."

But suddenly, a friend came to tell me his bad news.

So, I cried.

The doctor ran to me and said:

"Your fever is too high, you can't cry."

But how can I not cry!

The nurse ran to me and said:

"Your illness is very dangerous,

We don't allow you to be sad, we don't allow you to cry."

But how can I not cry!

We have not only lost a great teacher, a great comrade-in-arms,

But also lost the great spirit of the nation.

How can I not cry!

I cried all day, I cried all night,

The fever got higher, the breathing got faster,

Two nurses ran over to interfere with me severely!

"We don't allow you to cry!"

Using an ice pack to ice my head,

Using an ice pack to ice my chest.

They want to reduce my fever,

Want to cool my heart,

But how can I not cry! (October 20th, in the hospital)

Words in a Young Person's Heart

— Huang Yuan

Mr. Lu Xun is dead. Mr. Lu Xun has been dead for ten days. This is an undeniable fact. But can we believe it? No, absolutely not! I believe millions of young people will answer in unison: "No, absolutely not!"

Upon receiving the news of his death, I rushed to his bedside. It was two hours after he had stopped breathing. At that time, his hands were still warm. I gazed at him greedily. I seemed to see his chest still rising and falling. I knew it was an illusion. I kept this secret to myself. In the afternoon, the body was sent to the funeral parlor. The funeral parlor could not be occupied at night. When it was late, everyone had left, leaving only five of us young people to keep watch. At this time, the night was quiet and still. An upward-facing electric light in the room emitted a soft glow. Mr. Lu Xun slept peacefully and quietly on the bed surrounded by wreaths. Someone repeatedly said, "He is not dead. He is asleep. He seems like he will wake up and talk to us." When he was ill, he often lay down and talked to us. We all felt the same way.

In recent years, due to various reasons, although Mr. Lu Xun loved young people, he could not interact with them often. We were among the luckiest few of millions of young people, able to be close to Mr. Lu Xun and listen to his teachings. But this was our last opportunity to be close to him. I stood by the bed, touched his hand. His hand was cold. I wanted to look at him a few more times, to gaze at him greedily. I still seemed to see his chest rising and falling. I knew this was an illusion. I did not dare tell anyone. I kept this secret to myself.

The next day, the body was moved to the hall. From morning to night, it was crowded with young people paying their respects. They arrived with infinite grief. As soon as they stepped into the solemn hall, even seeing Mr. Lu Xun's body and portrait from afar, they could not hold back their tears. They may or may not have known Mr. Lu Xun, but their hearts of respect and grief were the same. It was not just respect and grief; after paying their respects, seeing Mr. Lu Xun, who had struggled bitterly all his life, lying quietly, knowing that the spirit of his bitter struggle now needed to be inherited by everyone, they felt anger and stepped out of the hall with resolute steps. I know that the spirit of Mr. Lu Xun lives in the heart of every young person and will blossom into magnificent and glorious flowers.

In the evening, more than six thousand young people came in with grief and left with resolute steps. The funeral hall became empty again. No, the funeral hall would not be empty and lonely. In just this one day, it had retained the deep grief and resolute heroism of more than six thousand young people.

The area in front of the coffin was piled with wreaths and flowers. Mr. Lu Xun slept peacefully in the flowers. The four of us young people accompanied Mr. Lu Xun and slept in the fragrance of the flowers. Before going to sleep, I quietly stood in front of Mr. Lu Xun's coffin, gazing at him greedily. I wanted to look at him a few more times. I saw his chest rising and falling again. I put my hand on my own chest, silently saying, "Mr. Lu Xun, your words are in my heart, and also in the hearts of millions of young people." But I still kept this secret to myself.

The next evening, Mr. Lu Xun's body was placed in a coffin with a glass lid, so that the upper part of his body was still visible. I silently stood in front of the coffin, gazing at him greedily. I wanted to look at him a few more times. I still saw his chest rising and falling. I could no longer keep this secret to myself. I called Yu and over and said to them:

"Look, Mr. Zhou seems to still be breathing."

They both said, "I also see that he seems to be breathing."

Could everyone be making the same mistake?

"No," I can say. Although Mr. Lu Xun's body is dead, his heart, his spirit, lives on, lives in the heart of each of us, lives in the hearts of millions of young people!

He Will Shout Forever

— Yi Fan

The impression Mr. Lu Xun's death gives us is not of death, but of fresh vitality. When his body was alive in the world, he did not let those he influenced come into contact with his colors and sounds every day. But after his death, his influence not only remains active in the hearts of every living person, but also lives more vividly and more truly. What died was only the body that a few of his friends could approach, but his unwavering spirit of resistance to inertia shines brightly among us and deeply penetrates all parts of the world.

In the midst of darkness and turmoil, we need light, we need friends. Mr. Lu Xun is the light that guides our modern youth, a friend to the masses. He shows us the direction, gives us courage, and teaches us to resist to the end. Young people all over the world need Mr. Lu Xun, and the young people of China especially need him. China does not lack writers, but it lacks tough, uncompromising, and unyielding writers like Mr. Lu Xun. Looking at the literary world in China, apart from those who specialize in talking about romance and using pornography to numb young people, there are some refined and humorous scholars who, after running several self-proclaimed pure and high-minded magazines in China, sell some of the so-called elegance of the Chinese people, the shortcomings of the Chinese people in the past, to foreign countries, flattering foreigners and making foreign money. There are also those who once stood among the masses and declared war on evil forces, but later, out of cowardice and selfishness, went to a friendly country to live as a pensioner. There are also those who, after encountering setbacks in their struggle, abandoned their careers and friends and went to live a secluded life. These are all considered writers, all considered living people, but some have been forgotten by us, and some have been discarded by us, and have died in our hearts. We need Mr. Lu Xun. Although we cannot keep him from the death of his body, his thoughts, his words and deeds, and the influence arising therefrom, will be more respected and more truly immortal among us than when he was alive.

Mr. Lu Xun once said: "My enemies are numerous. Let them hate. I will not forgive a single one." These words were not only spoken to his enemies, but also to his friends. Mr. Lu Xun is dead. His satirical and intolerant pen has been laid down. His sharp mouth has also been closed. But his friends all over the world will rise up after him, using their pens, their mouths, their fists, their teeth, their lives, to fight hand-to-hand with the unforgivable enemy. In this process, you and I can believe that it is Mr. Lu Xun himself. We will hear his shouts in all parts of the world and feel his unmistakable presence.

October 21.

Heartache

— Leng Mo

Heavy sorrow can lead to sudden, severe heartache. But a healthy person will hardly ever fall into such a situation easily. We often hear people say "why heartache," and some are just embellishments. Of course, this is just speculation. Assuming that one person should have the same feelings as another is not permissible, and assuming that two people are equally healthy is not easy to confirm accurately. As for myself, I feel that even presuming upon this point may not be right, but I believe that such presumption is by no means malicious. It is just a kind of admiration for healthy people. Because of circulatory problems that have plagued me for several years, my heartache is often easily triggered. Seeing models of diseases in the hospital will cause heartache, hearing the sirens of ambulances will cause heartache. Such worthless heartache, even when caused by sorrow, naturally does not indicate the depth of the sorrow. Only healthy people have the right to use heartache to express sorrow.

The sorrow of the weak is of course worthless, but it will continue shamelessly. Recently, my mind has been imprinted with phrases like "shortness of breath, unable to sleep, cardiac paralysis, sudden death." These phrases were obtained from the news of the death of a literary giant. For him, I will not say any commemorative words. My own worthless sorrow is naturally nothing to say. He certainly has many legacies that must be remembered, but some of his symptoms at the time of his death do not need to be remembered by others. Those words that are firmly imprinted in my mind have no meaning except for myself. Even the meaning for myself cannot be grasped in a concrete way. Is it because "Having grieved for the departed, I will reflect on myself"? I am not so decadent yet. Because I am not decadent, do I feel that the spirit of struggling heroically to the end still gives me a sense of encouragement? Then, the depressed mood caused by the disease no longer needs to be disguised. I know that I do not have the ability to turn a moan into another cry. Honestly, I even see a hint of pain in the healthy writing of others. Naturally, many of the great writer's works are written with extreme pain. But I strangely think that perhaps that luxury of pain is inherent in the disease. Could this be the meaning of my remembering the symptoms of the deceased?

Reading Chekhov's late works often brings to mind his appearance, tormented by illness. Reading other people's accounts of Chekhov's later life, he still tried his best to show calm and joy in his daily life, but in his own works, he could not help but naturally reveal his painful mood. This may not necessarily be unintentional, because he originally did not conceal his melancholic nature. Gorky, who suffered from the same disease as him, was completely without pessimism, but it cannot be said that his works do not contain elements formed by the disease. There are many places in his works that we cannot help but read with hurried breath, and I am afraid that the author wrote them in hurried breath. We do not need to pry into the disguise of suffering. Prying into it may be an insult to the work, but due to the psychology of the disease, we cannot help but regard it this way, and there is no way to avoid it. It is okay to say that this is an unhealthy idea. It is okay to say that this is an absurd idea. There is no need to reject this blame. Unless the deceased can add a little compassion to this mood, even in his lifetime, it would not be allowed.

Not long ago, a certain writer had an article expounding the psychology of the sick protagonist in one of his novels. This may have nothing to do with the writer himself, but the same type of protagonist appears repeatedly in the writer's various works, and it can be considered to reflect himself, or to reflect a certain real person. That protagonist has the characteristics of拼命工 (拼命工 - 'desperate worker', hard work), easy anger, and contempt for stupidity, etc., so his death becomes a conscious and inevitable death. The reader does not completely sympathize with this type of character, and it can be said that some people simply do not sympathize with him at all. However, if the author's opinion is allowed to be presumed, then this type of character is exactly the kind of character that the author uses to persuade people to sympathize with them. The reader's emotions do not correspond, because the factor of disease is ignored, so the author wants to specifically bring it up. However, after the author specifically brings it up, the healthy reader is afraid that he still cannot make any changes. The disease factor is too much regarded as mental, changeable, and people forget that it is material, irresistible. As for readers with similar diseases, even if the author does not mention the disease, they will feel it themselves, and they will also worry that the author is writing with the same sick mood. In this way, not only will they themselves have heartache, but they will also have heartache for the author and heartache for this type of character. This heartache can be said to be worthless, but I am afraid that there is always a reason that I cannot explain.

I do not know exactly to what extent lung disease can lead to heart abnormalities, and whether some patients only develop heart abnormalities at the end. Using the psychology of heart patients to pry into the psychology of lung patients is probably not suitable. But as long as the suffering is not completely different, then the presumption may not be entirely a misunderstanding. And that unnecessary memory has its own reasons for becoming a memory.

Silent Greatness

— Yi Bei

"I am like an ox, eating grass and squeezing out milk and blood." (Note 1)

Now, I feel even more the greatness of the ox. In the dim, cold dawn, treading on the frosty, cold earth, dragging the heavy iron plow, panting and breathing, quietly turning over the stubborn, barren soil, helping the seeds to grow, is the ox; and coming into the world to gnaw on dry, withered grass stalks, taking out priceless strength and nourishing milk and blood, all the way to death, is also the ox. But what makes us feel even more tragic is that even when panting and breathing, it still sincerely and silently squeezes out strength, milk, and blood. In this world of ours where we only hear people shouting "giving my all until my heart stops beating" and deceiving people, we can hardly imagine the sublimity of the ox.

But in this human world, "on the one hand, there is solemn work, and on the other hand, there is debauchery and shamelessness" (Note 2) – what else can be said? The regrettable thing is that even the wanton yapping of those tens of thousands of dogs cannot cover up the sublimity and greatness of the ox. It still makes us convinced that "no matter where, in the trivial self-enjoyment, there are people who want to comfort humanity; no matter in any era or in any country, there are rebels who raise their voices of resistance against the ugly and hateful reality. ... These rebels always end up pointing people to the road they should take, pushing people onto that road... It is breaking the work of those preachers who either make people compromise with the ugliness of the reality created by the old society or make people sink into ease and pleasure." (Note 3)

In our era, in our country, we have Mr. Lu Xun. He silently struggled with the baseness of humanity all his life - yes, it should be said that this "silent" greatness will forever shine brightly among us. He did not sigh once for being tired, "he did not know rest," and when he died, only from the mouth of his closest person did this wisp of tragic sound come out. Thinking of this, we cannot help but shed tears of tragic gratitude. Yes, Mr. Lu Xun should be said to be a great ox. His hardship is like that of an ox: he has also constantly dragged a heavy iron plow, treading the frozen long road in the dim, cold dawn, plowing the barren soil, and helping the lovely seeds on the ground to grow. "He eats grass and squeezes out milk and blood." But he is also different from the ox: his milk and blood never nourished the fat on the executioner's body - on the contrary, they poisoned them. His priceless and bitter milk and blood nourished the new generation of the future.

Now, this "great ox of great humanity" has left us forever. What remains in our hearts is a heavy and indelible dark shadow. Thinking of that great and tragic voice, I cannot help but cry bitterly. But we cannot forget those other base and joyful snickers hidden in the corners. Under the proclamation of the great "ox," can we use tears to answer the mocking snickers of the old world?

No - but let them say no more. Under the dim, cold dawn, the human world still retains thousands of miles of ridges and mountains. At this time, Mr. Lu Xun's death, for him and for us, is only full of unspeakable sorrow and regret.

However, we allow ourselves: we will always remember that great "ox" -

"He eats grass and squeezes out milk and blood."

(Note 1) Xu Guangping, Mr. Lu Xun's wife,述 (述 - 'narrate', 'describe') Lu Xun's words in Mr. Lu Xun's elegy.

(Note 2) See Ehrenburg: "The Last Byzantines."

(Note 3) M. Gorky: "My Literary Apprenticeship."

Mr. Lu Xun's Achievements in Language Reform

— Chu Yang

When enumerating Mr. Lu Xun's achievements in literature and the cultural movement, from the perspective of fundamental issues, his great contribution to language reform should be mentioned first. He was one of the first warriors of the "New Youth" to advocate vernacular Chinese. Looking at it today, he was the only person who fought tenaciously, persevered to the end, and strived for progress. Who among his contemporaries was not stagnant in the era and compromised with the old forces? Only Mr. Lu Xun, from advocating vernacular Chinese, attacking zombie literature, opposing scripture recitation and restoration, sweeping away "recorded sayings," to his most recent literary propositions, stood on the front line as a tenacious fighter. His influence is not only related to the changes and development of the entire nation's culture, but also paves the way for thousands of years to come.

Secondly: Mr. Lu Xun was also one of the earliest masters in establishing a new literary style. The emergence of the new-style novel in China began with his realistic work "Diary of a Madman" (published in 1918). His essays, which are called "a shot like a spear" or "miscellaneous essays," are unmatched in terms of quantity or quality. As for argumentative essays, Mr. Lu Xun once again created a unique style full of unique style and charm, sharp, cynical, scolding and cursing, filled with serious reason and surging passion.

In addition, Mr. Lu Xun's efforts in introducing foreign literary works from the earliest to the latest have resulted in the adoption of Western grammar, the habitual use of foreign loanwords, and the imitation of vocabulary... All efforts to increase the function of Chinese language and make up for its unscientific defects have been made to the best of his ability. If we carefully study his translations or works, we can discover many traces, some of which are even invisible, having been integrated into the literary web that he carefully created. It is these subtle creations that have great value and merit for the evolution of language and the learning of literary apprentices in the future.

If we only look at Mr. Lu Xun's work in language alone, we can feel that he has spent a lot of effort.

But the admirable and lovable thing about Mr. Lu Xun is that he saw his own and other people's strengths very clearly. He was never spiritually satisfied with what he pursued. "The world has no end, progress has no limit!" (Liang Rengong's words). Mr. Lu Xun was an extremely thorough evolutionist, a person with a dynamic worldview in essence. Even though he spent thirty years, day and night, pen in hand, he was never satisfied with his own articles written in words honed day and night, and constantly sought progress. It was in this state of dissatisfaction and desire for progress that he did his best, walked the path he should take, and also illuminated our path. We have received instructions from him. Let's see what he said:

"…I won't talk about others, but as for myself, it is true that I have read many old books. It is true that I am still reading them for teaching, so I am inevitably influenced by them and the sentences and structures of old Chinese are often revealed in my vernacular Chinese writing. But I am suffering from carrying these ancient ghosts on my back and cannot get rid of them, and I often feel a depressing heaviness... Mostly because of laziness, I often comfort myself that everything is in transition and there are always intermediate things. Between monocotyledons and dicotyledons, between invertebrates and vertebrates, there are intermediate things; or it can simply be said that in the chain of evolution, everything is an intermediate thing. When we first reformed writing, it was natural to have some authors who were neither fish nor fowl. It could only be like this, and it needed to be like this. Their task is to shout out a new voice after being somewhat alert; and because they come from the old camp, they see the situation more clearly and when they strike back, they should strike at the enemy's vitals. But they should still pass with time and gradually disappear, and at most they are just a piece of wood or stone in a bridge, not a target or model for the future. Those who follow should be different. If they are not naturally gifted, they cannot suddenly get rid of their accumulated habits, but they must have a newer look. In terms of literature, they do not need to make a living in old books, but should take the tongues of living people as a source, making articles closer to language and more vibrant. As for how to remedy the poverty and lack of the language of the people today and enrich it, that is also a big problem..."

Below he says: "I think that if I work hard enough, I can probably still collect spoken language to reform my writing, but because I am lazy and busy, I have not done it yet… (Lu Xun Selected Collection, page 64: Written Behind the Tomb)"

Did Mr. Lu Xun really not do it? Even if he didn't, it doesn't matter. He shouted out that he "came from the old camp, saw the situation more clearly, and attacked the enemy's vitals with ease." At least he has pointed out "the target for the future" to us.

Injury to the Thymus Gland: Preventing Aging and Reversing Aging Differentiated

— Translated by Dr. Chen Minbo, Graduate of the Medical Department of Tokyo Imperial University

Recognition of Italian Annexation

— Li Xuelian

A few days ago, the newspaper reported that other countries would recognize Italy's annexation of Abyssinia, as a wedge to form a European fascist front. This news became more and more confirmed after Italian Foreign Minister Ciano arrived in Berlin. On the 26th, according to news from the capital of Yugoslavia: "Reuters reported that the Yugoslav government will announce the recognition of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia within days. This step is in fact tantamount to Yugoslavia joining the sphere of influence of Italy and Germany." In this way, Germany's "recognition" has undoubtedly become a reality.

It is not surprising that Italy and Germany, two European fascist countries, are joining hands. Everyone is a country of aggressive militarism, clamoring to acquire new colonies. It goes without saying that Abyssinia was the first to become their victim; and it is also well known that many small European countries, as well as the fertile land of the Soviet Union, have subsequently become their "forbidden fruits." In order to acquire new colonies and re-divide the world, militaristic fascist countries naturally have to promote war. Their recent support for the Spanish rebels, which led to an international civil war, is one example.

Since World War I, people have become very tired of the inhuman war, and no one wants to cause these cruel war disasters again. Therefore, as the threat of World War II becomes increasingly urgent, the formation and increasing growth of the world's anti-war and anti-fascist movements to defend peace is also inevitable. The peace movement and the flames of war are two opposing situations, and they rise and fall with each other. Fascists have to create an atmosphere that promotes this crisis in order to expand the crisis of war. What is especially important is to form a fascist international organization—although they themselves often have contradictions, they turn into this possibility in certain common situations.

For this reason, it is extremely natural for Germany to use the recognition of Italy's annexation of Abyssinia to overcome the broken gap between the two fascist countries and to promote the smooth formation of the international fascist front. Although the recent dissolution of the Austrian Internal Guard has not been enough to affect the relationship between the two countries, it is still not enough to destroy this possibility. Yugoslavia's response to this "recognition" shows the international impact of the combination of these two fascist countries.

However, it does not seem to be a very clever means to promote the combination of the international fascist front at the expense of Abyssinia, because in this way, the "Manchukuo" in the Far East can be "recognized" in the same way, right?…………

The militarists in the Far East are gradually tending to fascism, and perhaps in the future, there will also be the possibility of joining the European fascist front? If so, then those who uphold peace will feel even more difficult, and the crisis of war will become even more tense. How will we save peace?—This is what we urgently need facts to answer. For this reason, we must especially consolidate our peace front.

The doors of the big mansion were opened, and many people were gathered outside, along with many carriages and sedan chairs. There were also many people like "Big Good Olds," swaying in and out of the doorway. Inside, looking deep within, there were musicians playing, and many strange, beautiful things to eat and play with. It was said to be the tenth birthday of the first "young master" of the Wang family in the "Wang Mansion"—Old Master Wang was over seventy years old and only had this one young master, making him incredibly rare.

At that time, my mother had said to me, "When we get better, when Son is ten years old, we'll have so many good things too."

No one understood the melancholy in my mother's words, weighed down by life; I, an eight-year-old child, firmly remembered that enticing phrase: ten years old!

Ten years old! But our days did not "get better" as my mother had hoped; on the contrary, they got worse day by day. The people in those "Eastern houses" were all so "indecent," not even comparable to the servants of the Wang Mansion across the street. Life was so difficult for them, and they had completely lost hope in life. The bald "Hui person" (Note: Muslim) who worked in the yarn factory and whose back was bent from working, would eat a bowl of cold rice and a three-copper-coin beef soup every night. He would then vent his anger with his woman, fighting, crying... The unemployed merchant next door who made fake "fortune tickets" would sneak home past midnight to sleep, afraid of being caught and imprisoned one day. The fresh fish seller would throw all the money he earned into "flower clubs," and when he lost money, he couldn't even pay the license fee. While doing business, he was arrested and locked up. Life had turned its back on them. Only the broker who worked for the XX person's cloth shop could live comfortably, sharing a building with his mistress. He would often open his mouth, revealing a row of ugly gold-inlaid teeth, and utter obscene, vulgar laughter...

In that year, when our lives had declined so much that it was disheartening, everyone couldn't help but look at that XX product's foreign cloth broker with a special—almost admiring—gaze. And I, having turned ten, relied on the "neighborly" relationship to be sent to that broker to "learn business." Every day, he would take me to the XX foreign cloth shop, where I would do nine hours of rough work like sweeping, wiping tables, and serving food, listening to those strange languages that sounded like birds chirping, which I could never understand.

It was at that time that the first cruel test of life fell upon me—and I was ten years old!—When they set up a peddler's stall and wanted me to follow the adults to call out sales in the alleys, an unbearable shame suffocated me. I refused to shout a single word, even to death. My face turned red.

"A child so stubborn! You need to be a bit courageous to make a living! So delicate, go be a young master! Will you shout or not: 'Mercerized foreign cloth, scratch-scratch call:...' Will you shout or not!"

I didn't shout—I finally didn't shout! But that night, when I went home, they beat me severely—I don't know when I was sent home—I seemed to see my mother crying by my side.

"I'm ten years old," I thought vaguely. However, the days passed, and my injuries eventually healed. Life was still as bad as ever, and the days were still as gray. But from then on, I didn't have to see that ugly smile with the gold teeth again. That year had passed; yes, I was ten years old.

But, "You need to be a bit courageous to make a living!" I thought maybe that was a bit right?

Frontier

— Yi Yi

Because of a slight delay at Yanshan, I was caught by the night not long after leaving there. The boundless wilderness was as if it had just crawled out of an inkwell, without a shred of light. The sky full of stars was also covered by dark clouds.

"See, see, isn't it late now? It's at least forty miles to Jiaodian... In this desolate wilderness, neither village ahead nor shop behind... God only knows what will happen!... " My old companion was nagging again, murmuring in a low voice, seemingly wanting me to hear, yet not wanting to say it outright. Thus, he vented his accumulated resentment on the horse, scolding sharply, the long whip cracking the heavy silence in the air. In this way, the tired horse, burdened by the pain, began to jolt violently a few times, but soon it returned to its slow pace, like a snail.

"Look, the sky is so overcast and the air is so stuffy. If it starts raining, and the mountain streams rush down, we'll really be in trouble!" The old companion slowly spoke, while lighting the mast lamp that was mostly blackened by smoke.

"Then hurry up a bit!"

"Hurry up a bit? Animals don't like walking in the dark. What's the use of hurrying! If we had delayed a little less, interfered a little less (meddling), we could have reached Jiaodian earlier... Humph, you didn't listen when I told you not to interfere! What happened? Wasn't it a live burial? Let me tell you, sir! A widow who steals a man must be buried alive. That's the custom in the frontier. Pity is pity, but what can you do!"

"This is too barbaric! Such things don't happen in the city!"

"Then you can only blame the countryside for being bad!"

Thus, the tragic scene of the live burial at Yanshan revolved in my mind: the village chief's ferocious face, the cold, indifferent faces of the onlookers, and the various taunts and vicious curses... That woman, that unfortunate woman with a pair of large, dark, and lively eyes, she made me admire her. I couldn't find a hint of fear on her face. Health and anger flushed her cheeks. She shouted loudly, "I did it! Because I am a woman! I want to do it... Come on, bury me! You shameless, shameless demons!..." Then she was knocked into the pit with that terrible blow. The village chief covered her with the first shovelful of dirt. On the other side, the young man was tied tightly to a tree. He endured the spitting and beating from any man or woman! He didn't say a word, nor did he cry out in pain. Finally, the village chief cut off one of his ears.—He was released... This terrible scene appeared one after another...

I glanced at my old companion. He was muttering something. The dim mast lamp couldn't break through the darkness, but it was the only light in this wilderness!

The cart moved dully, like a snail. No matter how angrily the whip cracked, it ignored it completely.

Suddenly, several sharp gunshots chased from the road behind. The drawn-out "shriek" seemed to cut several cracks in the darkness. The horse jumped wildly a few times and ran a few steps forward. The old driver twisted his body and said painfully, "It's over, it's over!..."

But what do we have? Thinking of this, I felt relieved. I peeked out from the gap in the cart cover. What was there besides darkness!

"Let fate decide!" The old driver slowly drove the horse, turning one ear towards the rear. We only breathed a sigh of relief after walking half a mile. But the cart had already been grabbed from behind by someone and couldn't move forward. I was surrounded by terror. I heard the person's rapid panting—

"Sir! Save me, I've been shot by bandits... Sir, I'm afraid they're still chasing me..."

Then, I felt relieved. The old driver stopped, picked up my walking stick, and jumped out of the cart very nimbly. I knew he was probably feigning, but the words of pain from that person had already proved that he was overthinking.

"It's you!..." The old driver exclaimed in surprise. When I jumped out of the cart and borrowed the light of the mast lamp, I saw clearly that he was the young man from Yanshan who had had his ear cut off.

"Yes... it's great that it's you... truly..." The young man unfolded a bitter smile on his blood-stained face. We helped him onto the cart. He pointed to his leg; he had been shot.

I was about to ask him why he had encountered bandits, but he waved his hand at the driver: "Drive quickly, don't let them catch up!" The old driver then grabbed the walking stick and hit the horse's buttocks one after another. The horse ran madly.

"Sirs!... "After a while, the young man said intermittently, "I truly love that woman, even though she had lost her husband... But she was buried alive like that for me! How heartbroken I am!... Alas! I was angry, I almost went crazy. I wanted to avenge her. So, I secretly ran to the village chief's house... I, I killed him!... I..." The young man buried his face in his hands and cried!

Silence fell. Only the old driver's heavy sigh could be heard, as well as the sound of the whip hitting the horse's buttocks.

Wu Sheng Society Broadcasts Play

Da Zhonghua (1160) 3:15 PM to 4:15 PM

Overture (Yi Yin Society) Vocal Performance (Manna) (Zhu Zhu)

Ah Q

He ran back to the Land God Temple in panic. The local bully, acting as an accomplice, stormed in. From then on, Ah Q added a layer of suffering from being searched and bankrupt. He didn't want to curse Master Zhao, he didn't blame the bully, nor could he blame Wu Ma. He only hated the small mouth of the laborer who received him. Although he had a fierce fight with the small mouth, it didn't help his life at all. Driven by hunger, he had to go to the Jingxiu Nunnery to steal the turnips of the weak, but it didn't help his future life either. So he had to say goodbye to his beloved hometown.

He went to the city to make a living with a male companion who shared the same fate. Although it was said that he was helping out at the Bai Xing's house, "Things are more expensive away from home, and people are cheaper in the countryside." The ridicule and oppression that Ah Q received from the people in his village were not necessarily reciprocated with affection and respect in the city. As for the old Master Bai, he would never be better than Master Zhao.

Ah Q, who was a good laborer who would harvest wheat when asked to harvest wheat, hull rice when asked to hull rice, row a boat when asked to row a boat, and chop wood when asked to chop wood, would also have the complaint of "being harsh to people and busy with work." Master Bai was not only not better than Master Zhao, but was even more cruel. Since Ah Q could not help out at the Bai's house, he certainly could not return home empty-handed, so he took a risk. The day he returned home in brocade robes, looking down on the village, although the villagers each held the mentality of "rather be respectful than slow," they would not misunderstand that Master Bai could have recruited Ah Q as his son-in-law out of love for talent, nor would they misunderstand that Ah Q could have picked up a piece of gold on the road.

Therefore, Ah Q, who was dressed in brocade, not only did not truly gain new respect, but made people even more afraid and wary of him. Master Zhao said in anger and shame...

However, even if the Zhao family had not been robbed, Ah Q could not escape the fate of being shot. Whether he was the mastermind of the robbery of the Zhao family by colluding with bandits was not really a problem.

Film

Mr. Ma Yanxiang's Impressions of the Soviet "Drama Festival"

— Hua

The largest theater can hold over ten thousand spectators. Established actors are at least thirty years old. The world-renowned Soviet "Drama Festival" has been held this year, and only Mr. Ma Yanxiang represented China for the first time this year. The Drama Festival has closed, and Mr. Ma has returned to China, bringing us, of course, some fresh materials regarding the arts.

The development of Soviet drama is a pioneer among the countries of the world, which is an undeniable fact. In terms of theaters, Moscow alone has more than sixty, all of which are state-run. The Soviet government's emphasis on art, the architecture of theaters, the spirit of actors, and everything else are all worth referring to by countries around the world. Everyone has such an impression in their minds. Yesterday, Mr. Ma arrived in Shanghai, and the writer had an occasional opportunity to meet him at his residence, asking him for his impressions of this Soviet Drama Festival. According to what he told us:

One: The "audience seating" in Soviet theaters is relatively large, accommodating tens of thousands of spectators, and the smallest can accommodate more than two thousand people. Every theatrical performance is "fully packed with audiences, mostly workers and farmers. This can be said to be unique in the world, but there is such a good phenomenon in the Soviet Union. The level of Soviet culture can be imagined. Now, in the Soviet Union, very few children over the age of eight are illiterate.

"Soviet actors are not perfunctory. For every script staged, the rehearsal time must be at least half a year. On the morning of the performance, regardless of whether the script has been performed before, it must be rehearsed once or twice more. Even if it is a familiar play that has been performed hundreds of times, the actors do not feel troubled. This is also a spirit that the world, at least my country, does not have.

"The training of an actor or the success of an actor is not a coincidence, nor can it be made into a star overnight through a few newspaper and magazine praises. Training an actor requires at least seven or eight years of stage experience, and at the same time, life experience also needs to be experienced before there is an opportunity to play a supporting role. Moreover, practical acting skills and theory must be constantly studied until death. An established actor in the Soviet Union is at least thirty years old, and so are actresses, which is not comparable to our country's emphasis on youth and beauty. (To be continued)

Joan Bennett and Zachary Scott Co-star in "Scandal in Paris" Showing at Grand Theatre

"Yi Hua" Gleanings

Yi Hua's new film "Guangling Tide" is a great masterpiece of revolutionary history, which has recently been completed. It was screened for the first time in the company's screening room yesterday, and it was praised as Chen Kengran's unprecedented contribution.

"Guangling Tide" is a great production with revolution as the warp and love as the weft. Yi Hua spent more than 80,000 yuan, truly sparing no expense. All the technical personnel were mobilized, breaking all records of domestic films. Stars such as Yuan Meiyun, Wang Yin, Lu Ming, Jiang Yiqiu, Guan Hongda, Liang Dusheng, etc., worked especially hard, and the results were particularly remarkable.

Fang Lin's "Sequel to Avatar Girl" and Xu Sulin's "Sea and Sky Lovers" are being worked on day and night, working hard, and are expected to be completed within the year.

Yue Feng expressed that he will write and direct a very realistic great film close to national defense, so that people can understand that he has not changed his past style. Chen Kengran will direct Pan Zigenong's "Elastic Children 1-", etc., after "Guangling Tide" is screened, it will start filming.
